1201 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Bradley


Civ. No. 31301


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


258 Cal. App. 2d 253; 65 Cal. Rptr. 570; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2410



January 25, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 20, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County sitting as a juvenile court. Edward J. Olstyn, Court Commissioner, Judge pro tem.

Action to declare a minor a ward of the court on the basis of a charge of reckless driving causing bodily injury.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment declaring minor to be a ward of the court, placing him under control and supervision of the probation officer in his parents' home, and suspending his driving license for six months affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant minor sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which declared the minor to be a ward of the court, placed him under control and supervision of plaintiff probation officer in his parents' home, and suspended his driving license for six months. The probation officer had filed an action to have the minor declared a ward of the court due to a charge of reckless driving causing bodily injury.


OVERVIEW: The evidence disclosed that the minor willfully and knowingly drover his vehicle at a high rate of speed directly toward a 14-year-old child in a game of chicken. The child froze with terror, was unable to move out of the direct path of the oncoming vehicle, and consequently was struck and seriously injured. Under the circumstances there was an abundance of evidence to support the trial court's conclusion that the minor intentionally drove his vehicle with knowledge that serious injury to the child was probable, or that he intentionally acted with a wanton and reckless disregard of the possible result of his conduct. The court also ruled that there was nothing in the applicable provisions of the Juvenile Court Law that offended the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments or Cal. Const. art. I, § 13. Under the Juvenile Court Law, the minor was afforded due process of law by review of the judgment of the juvenile court judge on appeal from the judgment rendered upon the rehearing. The minor's claim that Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 559 was unconstitutional because of its alleged vagueness and indefiniteness was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1202 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Dobbins


Civ. No. 31508


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


258 Cal. App. 2d 262; 65 Cal. Rptr. 704; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2411



January 25, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 23, 1968, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 20, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County sustaining an objection to the report of the inheritance tax appraiser and fixing the inheritance taxes. Joe Raycraft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Controller of the State of California challenged the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained the objection to an inheritance tax appraiser's report of respondent children of the decedent (children) and fixed inheritance taxes payable on interests that passed from the decedent to his children under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 13693 (1965).


OVERVIEW: The decedent's father left part of his estate in trust to the decedent, giving the decedent a power of appointment over the trust assets. The decedent's will had a provision in case any child predeceased him. The trust assets were distributed to the children by a court order that made no reference to the decedent's will. The appraiser's report included as a taxable transfer by the decedent to the children one-fourth of the market value of the assets held in the trust. After the trial court sustained the children's objection and ruled that the assets were not transferred subject to the inheritance tax law, the controller appealed. The court affirmed. To the extent that the decedent attempted to appoint the trust property other than to his children living at the date of his death in fee simple absolute, the appointment was a nullity and was not regarded as effecting a transfer subject to inheritance tax. The power of appointment was a limited power, rendering moot any question as to general powers of appointment. The exercise of a power which did not change the estates vested in persons who would take on a failure to exercise the power was not a transfer subject to inheritance tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which sustained the children's objection to the tax appraiser's report and fixed the inheritance taxes.

 

1203 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Kramer v. Boynton


Civ. No. 30928


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


258 Cal. App. 2d 171; 65 Cal. Rptr. 669; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2403



January 23, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On February 14, 1968, the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 20, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County granting a new trial to plaintiff after jury verdict favoring defendant. Leonard A. Diether, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted plaintiff's motion for a new trial following a jury verdict in favor of defendant in plaintiff's action for battery.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff and defendant became involved in an altercation at work. Plaintiff claimed at trial that defendant struck plaintiff without provocation. Defendant claimed that he struck plaintiff in self defense. After the jury found for defendant, the trial court granted plaintiff's motion for a new trial on the ground that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict. Affirming that decision, the court applied the mandate of Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 657 to reverse only if the record contained "no substantial basis" for the trial court's stated reasons and ruled that the trial court was entitled to weigh the evidence and believe plaintiff's account of the events, a version that did not justify the battery, in reaching its conclusion that the jury should have reached a different verdict. The court rejected defendant's argument that the verdict could have been based on the jury's belief that plaintiff suffered no damages and that § 657 required the trial court to include a record of its belief that plaintiff was damaged. The court determined that § 657 did not require the trial to set forth each and every step of its reasoning that led it to grant the motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1204 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brim


Crim. No. 2914


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


257 Cal. App. 2d 839; 65 Cal. Rptr. 265; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2513



January 15, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 13, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. William P. Mahedy, Judge.

Prosecution for being in a place where narcotics were being unlawfully smoked or used with knowledge of such activity.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction for the crime of being in a place where narcotics were being unlawfully smoked or used with knowledge of such activity, in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11556, that was entered by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California).


OVERVIEW: In his nonjury trial, defendant was also acquitted of the charge of possession of marijuana, in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence that defendant smoked marijuana in his apartment two weeks prior to the charged incident. The court rejected defendant's argument. The court noted that the evidence was introduced at the preliminary examination and, knowing of the admission, defendant agreed to the submission of the case on the transcript from the preliminary examination. The court also observed that the evidence was admissible to show guilty knowledge, as required under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11556. The court further ruled that the acquittal of defendant and all others present in the apartment of possession charges did not require an acquittal of the charge under § 11556. The court emphasized that § 11556 did not require proof of possession. Moreover, the evidence of the presence of marijuana and a strong odor of burning marijuana when officers arrived at defendant's apartment was sufficient to establish that marijuana was unlawfully smoked in his presence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1205 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Aguiar


Crim. No. 6174


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


257 Cal. App. 2d 597; 65 Cal. Rptr. 171; 1968 Cal. App. LEXIS 2484



January 4, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 28, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. W. Howard Hartley, Judge.

Prosecution for possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which convicted him of possession of marijuana under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that § 11530 was unconstitutional under the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed his conviction. The court concluded that the state could punish the possession of marijuana for private use and that § 11530 was constitutional. The court held that the desirability of the social policy underlying the statute was a purely legislative matter and that it was improper for the court to weigh fact-finding studies against each other. Some studies reported that the use of marijuana, once begun, led to excess, while other studies reported no ill effects of marijuana use. The court found that the accused made no showing that any wrongful discrimination or other impure motive existed for the alleged disparity between the treatment of alcohol and marijuana.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana.

 

1206 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Baruch Inv. Co. v. Huntoon


Civ. No. 24192


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


257 Cal. App. 2d 485; 65 Cal. Rptr. 131; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1805



December 27, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 21, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. John Stuart Frazer, Judge.

Action to recover for a breach of an agreement under which a defendant used its accounts receivable to obtain working capital and cross-action for usury.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants and cross-complainants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lender challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied it recovery for breach of an agreement under which respondent borrower used its accounts receivable in order to obtain working capital. The trial court also awarded the borrower damages on its cross-complaint for usury. The lender had withheld a reserve of 30 percent of the accounts on several occasions.


OVERVIEW: The lender contended that Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22 violated the equal protection clause of the United States Constitution. Section 22 provided that the rate of interest upon any loan was to be seven percent per annum, and also provided that parties could contract in writing for a rate not exceeding ten percent. The lender also asserted that the treble damages and misdemeanor provisions of the usury law, Cal. Gen. Laws § 3 (1918), discriminated by penalizing some classes, but not others, for identical acts. The court held that: (1) the lender lacked standing to attack the constitutionality of the usury law because the lender had not sustained and was not in immediate danger of sustaining any direct injury as the result of the usury law's enforcement; and (2) the transaction was an open loan account masquerading as a sale of accounts, which enabled the borrower to procure compensation in excess of the lawful ten percent per annum for the use and forbearance of money. The assignment of the invoices and evidences of debt constituted a pledge for security; thus, the lender's rights terminated when the borrower repaid all sums advanced with the lawful amount of interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the borrower.

 

1207 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. De La Torre


Crim. No. 14309


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


257 Cal. App. 2d 162; 64 Cal. Rptr. 804; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1765



December 19, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 14, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Municipal Court for the East Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County, dismissing a complaint. Myer B. Marion, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed from an order of the Municipal Court for the East Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County (California) granting defendant's motion to dismiss on the ground that Cal. Veh. Code § 2814 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Upholding the constitutionality of Cal. Veh. Code § 2814, which required the driver of a passenger vehicle to stop and submit his vehicle to a mechanical inspection where members of the California Highway Patrol were conducting tests and inspections and when signs were displayed requiring such stop, the court reinstated the complaint against defendant charging him with driving while under the influence of an intoxicating liquor. The state could practice preventative therapy through the use of reasonable road checks to ascertain whether drivers and automobiles met the legislative determination of fitness. Defendant's right of mobility was not inalienable, and there had to always be a logical appreciation of the demands of public safety to which an individual's rights and liberties had to yield when balanced against a right that was not fundamental but merely involved a slight inconvenience. The enjoyment of many personal rights and freedoms were subject to restraint under the police power of the state, which restraint might include reasonable conditions to insure the safety, good order, and public welfare of the people.


OUTCOME: The order of dismissal was reversed and the cause remanded to the trial court with instructions to reinstate the proceedings.

 

1208 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Mid-Way Cabinet Fixture Mfg. v. County of San Joaquin


Civ. No. 11732


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


257 Cal. App. 2d 181; 65 Cal. Rptr. 37; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1768



December 19, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 15, 1968, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 14, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County. William Biddick, Jr., Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel San Joaquin County and its planning director to grant a use permit for building purposes minus allegedly invalid conditions imposed by the county.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County (California) in favor of defendants, County of San Joaquin and its planning director, which denied the company's petition for mandate to compel the county and its planning director to grant a use permit for building purposes minus allegedly invalid conditions imposed by the county.


OVERVIEW: The company sought a use permit to construct an addition. The county, at the suggestion of its planning department, conditioned the granting of the use permit on conveyance to the county of certain of the company's interests in real estate. The county and planning director argued that whenever a zoning ordinance, and particularly the "use permit" granting or withholding power therein written permitted, the granting of a use permit should have been conditioned upon free conveyances. The court found that the purpose which the county and planning director sought to accomplish, shifting the burden of the cost of access and highway widening rights of way and the cost of interchanges onto adjoining landowners, was not the purpose for which zoning ordinances were properly designed. The county and planning director claimed to have been exercising police power, but the court found they were improperly exercising eminent domain.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and directed the trial court to issue the peremptory writ.

 

1209 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Doctor


Crim. No. 14322


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


257 Cal. App. 2d 105; 64 Cal. Rptr. 608; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1759; 33 Cal. Comp. Cases 804



December 18, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Municipal Court for the San Antonio Judicial District of Los Angeles County dismissing an amended complaint charging a failure to secure payment of workmen's compensation. Alfred W. Dibb, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellate department of the superior court (California) certified the appeal filed by the state, to resolve the issue whether an accusatory pleading, filed more than one year after commission of the offence of failing to secure the payment of compensation, a misdemeanor under Cal. Lab. Code § 3710.2, had to set forth the date of discovery and facts which show that the offense could not have been earlier discovered.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the misdemeanor of failing to provide worker's compensation coverage. The trial court dismissed the complaint because it was brought more than one year after the date of the offense. The court adopted the opinion of the intermediate appellate court and ruled that the accusatory document was required to state facts which would set forth not only the date of discovery but also would show why, by the use of due diligence, the offense could not have been earlier discovered. In order to comply with the speedy trial and due process clauses, a prosecution for a misdemeanor had to be brought within one year of the date of the offense. This statute of limitations went to jurisdiction, rather than merely to remedy. Because violations of the worker's compensation laws were equated to a case of fraud, the court read into the statute a duty to exercise diligence to discover the facts that constituted the fraud. Thus, the state had to plead and prove lack of knowledge, lack of means of obtaining knowledge, and when and how the fraud was discovered.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the amended complaint was reversed with directions to the trial court to permit the state to file a further amended complaint to state facts why the offense could not have been earlier discovered.

 

1210 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Nash


Civ. No. 31569


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


256 Cal. App. 2d 560; 64 Cal. Rptr. 298; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1886; 27 A.L.R.3d 1349



November 30, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 27, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County fixing an inheritance tax on a portion of an estate. Florence M. North, Court Commissioner, Judge pro tem.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) fixing an inheritance tax on a portion of an estate pursuant to Cal. Prob. Code § 1240. Respondent, the State Controller, opposed the action of the administrator seeking a modification of the order fixing the tax.


OVERVIEW: The testatrix's sister and her sister's husband rejected by a written instrument a remainder interest in the residue of the testatrix's estate. They also rescinded their prior assignment for value of this interest to the life tenant of the interest, the testatrix's husband. The trial court, applying Cal. Rev. and Tax. Code § 13409, fixed the tax in accordance with the report and as if the bequest had not been rejected. The administrator argued that the rejection of the bequest, which ordinarily would have related back to the time of the testatrix's death to prevent vesting of the legacy, created an intestacy with respect to the interest, and that since the entire estate was community property, such interest then passed intestate to the testatrix's surviving husband. The court disagreed. The court found that under § 13409, the rejection of the bequest was merely a renunciation of rights under the will and that § 13409 prevented the renunciation from relating back for inheritance tax purposes. The court noted that the inheritance tax did not deprive a taxpayer of his property without due process of law because the right of inheritance was entirely statutory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order fixing the inheritance tax.

 

1211 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Roberts


Crim. No. 6062


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


256 Cal. App. 2d 488; 64 Cal. Rptr. 70; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1877



November 29, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Monterey County suspending imposition of a sentence and granting probation on certain conditions to a defendant in a prosecution for unnatural sex behavior. Clyde H. Larimer, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of engaging in unnatural sex behavior in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288a. He appealed an order from the Superior Court of Monterey County (California) suspending imposition of sentence and granting probation on certain conditions.


OVERVIEW: While investigating homosexual activity in a park's public rest room, two police officers drilled peepholes in a wall of the men's restroom so that they could see the public portion of the rest room. Defendant was arrested after the officers allegedly witnessed him engaging in homosexual activities. The court overturned the order. First, the court held that when the case against a defendant was a close one, an error which otherwise would not be prejudicial might justify a new trial. Here, the case was a close one in part because of the officers' difficulties in observing suspects through the peepholes. Second, the court held that the trial court committed prejudicial error when it refused to give defendant's requested instruction to the effect that if the jury had a reasonable doubt as to whether the police officers could identify defendant from their place of concealment, the jury should acquit him. Where, as here, an additional reasonable doubt instruction which pointed to the theory of the defense was requested, it was error to refuse to give it, notwithstanding Cal. Penal Code § 1096a. Finally, the court rejected defendant's argument that § 288a was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

 

1212 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Hidden Valley Municipal Water Dist.


Civ. No. 29759


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


256 Cal. App. 2d 271; 63 Cal. Rptr. 889; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1853



November 22, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 17, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Ventura County. Louis C. Drapeau, Judge. *


* Retired Justice of the Court of Appeal sitting under assignment by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a water district to grant petitions which would exclude certain lands from the district or in the alternative would consent to the annexation of same lands to another water district.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting peremptory writ reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant water district appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which directed the issuance of a peremptory writ of mandate setting aside an earlier decision that denied the petition of plaintiff residents for exclusion of their lands from the district and annexing them to a different district.


OVERVIEW: Water district had been formed to preserve a community's way of life and to prevent it from being included in an adjoining water district. The district initiated successful injunctive proceedings to prevent its annexation by the adjoining district. However, district's ground-water supply was inadequate and the property owners proposed excluding their land from the district. The district's board denied the petition. The property owners appealed and the lower court found in their favor, finding that insufficient reason had been provided by the board in its denial. The water district appealed and the court reversed. The court held that this kind of district was normally formed and maintained for the purpose of bettering either the water supply or the water service, or both, within its boundaries and that the water district had not done so. The court found that as quasi-judicial proceedings, the district's hearings were fair and that the quasi-legislative policy the board adhered to in its decision against the property owners did not discriminate against them. The court found that district merely refused to exempt the property owners from its fundamental water policy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court, which had directed the issuance of a peremptory writ of mandate setting aside an earlier decision that denied residents' petition for exclusion of their lands from the district and annexing them to a different district.

 

1213 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Reimel v. Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board


Civ. No. 22905


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


256 Cal. App. 2d 158; 64 Cal. Rptr. 26; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1839



November 21, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 256 Cal. App. 2d 158 at 176.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to review decisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board revoking decisions of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control to suspend and revoke several liquor licenses for alleged violation of minimum price fair trade regulations.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgments denying writs reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff department of alcoholic beverage control (department) sought review of the decisions of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied the department's motions seeking reversal of the decisions of defendant appeals board, which revoked the department's decisions to suspend and revoke several liquor licenses held by defendant license holders for alleged violations of minimum fair trade regulations.


OVERVIEW: The license holders held off-sale general liquor licenses issued by the department. The department filed accusations alleging that the license holders sold branded distilled spirits at prices less than the stipulated minimum retail schedules duly filed with the department. The court reversed the trial court's decision denying the department's motions seeking reversal of the appeal board's decisions, which revoked the department's decisions to suspend and revoke several of the liquor licenses because of the violation. Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24755 and Rule 99(k), Cal. Code Regs. tit. IV, § 99(k), provided that the department was to publish the schedule. Strict liability was imposed on those exercising the privilege of selling alcoholic beverages. Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24875, which related to minimum price schedules for wine, specifically designated publishing in a trade journal. There was no indication that the legislature intended publication to mean personal notice. There was nothing illegal about the claimed compulsion to subscribe to a private trade journal because all statute-directed publications of notice were made in privately owned newspapers or journals.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision denying the department's motions seeking reversal of the decisions of the appeals board, which revoked the department's decisions to suspend and revoke several liquor licenses held by the license holders for alleged violations of minimum fair trade regulations.

 

1214 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Powers v. Floersheim


Civ. No. 29934


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


256 Cal. App. 2d 223; 63 Cal. Rptr. 913; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1846



November 21, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 11, 1967, and the Petition of the Defendants and Appellants for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 17, 1968. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred Gitelson, Judge.

Action in injunctive relief to restrain defendants from engaging in business as a collection agency until they are licensed to do so.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment enjoining defendants from performing certain services in conjunction with sales of forms reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, corporations, owners, salespersons, and clerk (corporations), appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that they were enjoined from selling collection forms that were accompanied by added services. Plaintiff state agency appealed the trial court's order enjoining the state agency from taking action to stop the sale of collection forms that were not accompanied by services.


OVERVIEW: The unlicensed corporations sold collection forms that were marketed to creditors as an effective way of collecting debts. The corporations also performed mail forwarding and addressing services as a way of enhancing the effectiveness of the forms. The trial court held that the sale of the collection forms when accompanied by forwarding and addressing services by unlicensed entities violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6853 of the Collection Agency Act (Act), but that when the forms were not accompanied by services that there was no violation. The court affirmed the trial court's findings that the corporations violated the Act and reversed the trial court's holding that the mere selling of forms did not violate the Act. The court held that because the corporations represented their forms as an effective means of collecting debts, the corporations were involved in a collection scheme in violation of § 6853 even when they were only selling forms. Because none of the forms contained any expressions of thought, the court held that the corporations' free speech rights were not violated by § 6853 and that the state agency was permitted to enjoin all sales of the collection forms.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the sale of collection forms accompanied by services violated the Act and reversed the trial court's decision to the extent that it held that the sale of collection forms not accompanied by services did not violate the Act. The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to enter an injunction in conformity with the court's opinion.

 

1215 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Breshears v. Indiana Lumbermens Mut. Ins. Co.


Civ. No. 800


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


256 Cal. App. 2d 245; 63 Cal. Rptr. 879; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1849



November 21, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Charles W. Johnson, Judge.

Action in declaratory relief to determine whether recovery can be made under an "open" fire insurance policy for the additional cost of reconstructing in compliance with changed building codes.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiff reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) allowing for increased costs of reconstructing a fire-damaged building in an action seeking declaratory relief in connection with Cal. Ins. Code §§ 411, 412, 2051, 2070, and 2071.


OVERVIEW: A fire occurred in a building owned by respondent causing damage. At the time of fire the dwelling was insured by appellant under an "open" fire insurance policy. The policy was in substantial compliance with the standard form prescribed by Cal. Ins. Code § 2071. Appellant contested estimates for repair which included costs brought about by changes made in building codes after the building was constructed but before the insurance policy was issued. The trial court allowed increased costs and held the provision of § 2071 which disallows such costs was unconstitutional as violative of the equal protection clause. On appeal the court found § 2071 was not unconstitutional as the plain language of the statute showed it afforded uniform and equal protection to all building owners under an "indemnity" concept of insurance. Also, recovery for additional costs for reconstructing in compliance with changed building codes was disallowed under § 2051.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as the insurance code provision was not unconstitutional and the measure of indemnity was the expense of replacing the thing lost or injured in its condition at the time of injury.

 

1216 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Smith-Rice Heavy Lifts, Inc. v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 30256


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


256 Cal. App. 2d 190; 63 Cal. Rptr. 841; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1842



November 21, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 12, 1967, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 17, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Beach Vasey, Judge.

Action for recovery of ad valorem property taxes paid on the commercial use of three barges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying recovery affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied the taxpayers recovery of ad valorem property taxes paid to respondent county on the commercial use of three barges.


OVERVIEW: The lower court denied the taxpayers recovery of ad valorem property taxes on certain derrick barges because it found that the barges were not engaged in the transportation of freight. On appeal, the taxpayers argued that they were entitled to tax exempt status under Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 4 and that the county could not assess the tax by virtue of Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §§ 1139, 1140. The court affirmed the lower court judgment because §§ 1139, 1140 were properly interpreted and did not preclude taxation of the barges by the county. The court found that in the years preceding the case the taxpayers' barges had been physically within the county and had received the benefit of fire and police services therefrom. The taxpayers failed to sustain their burden of proof to show that the tax assessment was unauthorized by law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment that denied the taxpayers recovery of the ad valorem property taxes paid to the county on certain barges.

 

1217 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Chavez v. Municipal Court of Visalia Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 776


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


256 Cal. App. 2d 149; 64 Cal. Rptr. 76; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1838



November 20, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 13, 1967, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 17, 1968. McComb, J., and Burke, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County. John Locke, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain the Justice Court of the Porterville Judicial District from proceeding in a criminal action.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ reversed with directions to issue writ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order from the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), which denied a writ of prohibition filed by appellant to restrain the county justice court from proceeding in a criminal action on the basis that the charging statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged in the justice court with the illegal use of a speaker mounted on a vehicle, in violation of a county loud speaker control ordinance. Appellant demurred to the complaint, which was overruled. Appellant petitioned the superior court for a writ of prohibition, which was denied. On review, the court reversed judgment with directions to the superior court to issue the writ. The court held that the county ordinance was unconstitutional because it was not a reasonable exercise of police power and presented too much opportunity for discrimination, political preference, and censorship, which was repugnant to a democratic society. Further, the application process for a permit under the ordinance was prone to delay tactics, which was detrimental to freedom of speech. The court recognized that while the state and its subdivisions had the sovereign right to protect the lives, privacy, and property of citizens, and had wide discretion in exercising police power, statutes involving the police power could be declared unconstitutional when they were arbitrary or unreasonable attempts to interfere with the basic rights guaranteed by the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of appellant with directions to the trial court to issue the writ of prohibition and dismiss a criminal charge against appellant.

 

1218 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gonzales


Crim. No. 12776


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


256 Cal. App. 2d 50; 63 Cal. Rptr. 581; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1825



November 16, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 8, 1968. Tobriner, J., and Mosk, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County committing defendant to a narcotics rehabilitation facility and from orders denying a motion for dismissal. William B. Keene, Judge, and Edward J. Olstyn, Court Commissioner, Judge pro tem.



DISPOSITION: Order of commitment affirmed; appeal from orders denying motion dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged orders of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which committed him, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 3102, to a narcotics rehabilitation facility and denied his motion for dismissal. Appellant challenged the legality of his arrest, not the validity of the commitment proceeding or asserted lack of jurisdiction of the trial court to institute the commitment proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's motions to dismiss were denied and the trial court found him to be a narcotic addict under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 3100. Appellant was committed to a rehabilitation facility. Appellant contended that his arrest was illegal and, therefore, his commitment should be set aside. On appeal, the court affirmed the commitment and denial of appellant's motions to dismiss. The court concluded that there was no illegal search or seizure relevant to appellant and that there was probable cause to arrest appellant based on what officers saw in plain view. Further, the commitment proceeding was civil in nature, not criminal, and, the exclusionary rules applicable to criminal cases were not controlling. The sole issue at trial was whether appellant was a drug addict or, by reason of repeated use of narcotics, was in imminent danger of becoming addicted. The procedural requirements for commitment were strictly followed. Thus, the jurisdiction of the trial court was unaffected by the legality of the arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order of commitment to a narcotics rehabilitation facility. The court also affirmed the orders, which had denied defendant's motions to dismiss, and the court dismissed defendant's appeals from those denial orders.

 

1219 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Northern


Crim. No. 12853


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


256 Cal. App. 2d 28; 64 Cal. Rptr. 15; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1822



November 15, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 11, 1968.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. John G. Barnes, Judge.

Prosecution for the illegal sale of marijuana and for illegal sale of a substance falsely represented to be marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for the sale of marijuana, a violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11531, and the sale of a substance falsely represented to be a narcotic, a violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11503, in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California). Defendant argued that remarks of the prosecutor violated defendant's Fifth Amendment right against self incrimination and that jury instructions were improper.


OVERVIEW: An undercover officer bought a cigarette containing marijuana from defendant, and about a week later, the officer bought a second package from defendant that defendant represented was marijuana. When tested by a chemist, the substance was not a narcotic. Defendant was charged and convicted of violations of Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 11531 and 11503. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. A remark by the prosecutor appeared to be a direct reference to defendant's failure to take the witness stand. However, there was no reasonable doubt that the prosecutor's comment did not contribute to defendant's conviction. It was immaterial to a violation of § 11503 whether defendant, either before or at the time of the delivery of the non-narcotic substance, intended to deliver a narcotic or some innocuous material. Section 11503 was violated if there was an offer of a narcotic and a subsequent delivery of a non-narcotic substance. Accordingly, defendant suffered no disadvantage when the trial court imposed the additional requirement of an intent to furnish a narcotic or when it failed to instruct that fraudulent intent was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1220 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Department of Water Resources v. Brown


Civ. No. 804


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


255 Cal. App. 2d 597; 63 Cal. Rptr. 363; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1317



November 1, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 27, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County. Jean Morony, Judge.

Proceeding in eminent domain to condemn land for the use of the rocks and gravel on it, and eventually for fish and wildlife preservation and recreation purposes.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment awarding allegedly inadequate damages affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County (California), which allegedly awarded inadequate damages in a proceeding in eminent domain that was brought by respondent California Department of Water Resources to condemn land for the use of the rocks and gravel on it, and eventually for fish and wildlife preservation and recreation purposes.


OVERVIEW: The owners' land was condemned by the Department for the avowed purpose of first removing the dredger tailings for use in the embankment of a dam, and eventually for fish and wildlife preservation and recreation purposes. The trial court refused to permit the trier of fact to consider the impact of the proposed project in determining the fair market value of the property being condemned. The trial court awarded damages that the owners alleged were inadequate. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that the beneficial purpose to be derived by the Department's use of the property was not to be taken into consideration in determining market values for it was wholly irrelevant. The court ruled that compensation was based on loss imposed on the owners rather than on benefit received by the Department. The court held that the owners were not entitled to recover attorneys fees because attorneys fees and expenses were not recoverable in a condemnation action except where provided for by statute, such as upon abandonment by the condemnor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1221 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Whelchel


Crim. No. 2812


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


255 Cal. App. 2d 455; 63 Cal. Rptr. 258; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1294



October 27, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from orders of the Superior Court of San Diego County committing defendants to the narcotic addict rehabilitation program as persons in imminent danger of becoming narcotic addicts. Verne O. Warner, Eli H. Levenson and Ronald Abernethy, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant committees appealed from orders of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) committing them under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 3050 to a narcotic addict rehabilitation program as persons in imminent danger of becoming narcotic addicts.


OVERVIEW: The committees were convicted in a municipal court of a drug possession offense and were certified to the trial court for a determination of whether they were addicted or in imminent danger of becoming addicted to narcotics. Two doctors were appointed to examine them, and counsel was also assigned. One doctor testified at a preliminary hearing that they were in imminent danger of becoming addicted to narcotics, and both doctors signed a certificate to that effect. The committees then demanded a jury trial, at which they were called as witnesses to testify against themselves. The trial court committed them. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not sufficiently comply with Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5564 because both doctors who signed the commitment certificate did not testify as required. The trial court's failure to inform the committees that they had a right to present their defense was immaterial because an attorney had been appointed to represent them who told them of the right. Because the commitment was a civil action, not a criminal one, the court rejected the committees' complaints that they were unconstitutionally forced to testify.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the commitments with instructions to the trial court to conduct the proceedings instituted by the certification from the municipal court in accord with the law and the facts and in harmony with the view expressed in the court's opinion.

 

1222 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Amar


Civ. No. 31777


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


255 Cal. App. 2d 404; 63 Cal. Rptr. 444; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1288



October 26, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred J. McCourtney, Judge.

Action to recover a further amount of inheritance tax to be paid under Rev. & Tax. Code, § 13441.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for petitioner affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant objectors sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found in favor of respondent, the California State Controller. The Controller filed the action to recover a further amount of inheritance tax to be paid under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 13441.


OVERVIEW: A decedent's will was admitted to probate. A state inheritance tax appraisement and report were made and approved. The amount was paid. Thereafter, a federal estate tax return was made, and the amount of state tax actually paid was allowed as a credit against the federal amount due. A state inheritance tax appraiser then filed a "supplemental" report, claiming a further amount due under § 13441, which allowed for an "additional" or "pickup" tax by which the state could take advantage of a revenue raising opportunity. Under § 13441, if an amount allowable was more than what was paid to the state, the difference was imposed as an additional tax. There was no increased liability. Rather, the amount payable to the federal government was instead payable to the state. The objectors challenged the procedural device invoked for the collection of the tax, arguing that the state tax should not have been imposed until after the final determination of the federal tax. The court found, however, that when the estate was valued for federal tax, notification and tender of the amount of any additional tax was to be made and then paid to the state and claimed as a credit against the federal tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1223 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Tetreault v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 24099


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


255 Cal. App. 2d 277; 63 Cal. Rptr. 326; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1272



October 23, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Gerald S. Levin, Judge.

Action for refund of personal income taxes paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment disallowing deduction or tax credit for foreign income taxes affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) in favor of defendant Franchise Tax Board (board), denying them a refund of personal income taxes paid under protest to the state, following disallowance by the board of a deduction or a tax credit for certain Japanese income taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, a husband and wife residing and domiciled in California, claimed that Cal. Rev. & Tax Code §§ 17204 and 18001, which respectively denied the deduction and credit, were unconstitutional. The husband was a partner in a law firm with offices in San Francisco and Tokyo. In the California income tax returns for the years at issue, the taxpayers reported their proportionate share of the net income derived from the partnership's Japanese office. Under the law of Japan, an income tax was imposed on the net income derived from the Japanese office. The tax was withheld from clients' payments and sent directly to the Japan revenue office. The court affirmed the trial court judgment. The disallowance of a deduction or credit for taxes paid to a foreign nation was valid under the state constitution in that it was not contrary to any express constitutional provision. The disallowance also did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, the Commerce Clause, or any other provision of the United States Constitution. Finally, the statutes were not in violation of any treaty between Japan and the United States.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment disallowing deduction or tax credit for foreign income taxes paid by the taxpayers.

 

1224 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Montoya


Crim. No. 6016


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


255 Cal. App. 2d 137; 63 Cal. Rptr. 73; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1251



October 18, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 13, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Raymond J. Arata, Judge.

Prosecution for robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which convicted him of robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion to exclude all of the prosecution's evidence was denied by the trial court. In seeking review, defendant claimed that the motion should have been granted. Defendant argued that the arrest warrant was invalid as it failed to meet the requirements of particularity in describing the person to be seized, as prescribed by Cal. Const. art. 1, § 19, as well as by the Fourth Amendment, and further that it failed to state the time of its issuance as required by Cal. Penal Code § 815. On appeal, the court held that the description of defendant in the warrant did not meet the constitutional requirement and that the warrant was void for that reason. However, the court determined that it did not follow that defendant's arrest was unlawful simply because the warrant underlying it was void. The court found that Cal. Penal Code § 850 provided that the teletype of the warrant had the same legal effect as the original and that the teletype contained more information and facts than the warrant. The court determined that the officers had sufficient probable cause for the arrest of defendant even without the warrant, holding that the subsequent arrest and search were lawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant.

 

1225 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Long v. City of Anaheim


Civ. No. 8310


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


255 Cal. App. 2d 191; 63 Cal. Rptr. 56; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1259



October 18, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Joseph T. Ciano, Judge.

Action to restrain and enjoin the cities of Anaheim and Garden Grove from requiring plaintiffs to secure a business license to distribute and sell a newspaper published by the Socialist Labor Party.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying injunction reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff socialist labor party members filed an action against defendant cities to restrain and enjoin them from requiring the party members to secure a business license to distribute and sell their party newspaper. The Superior Court of Orange County (California) entered a judgment in favor of the cities and denied the party members' request for injunctive relief. The party members appealed.


OVERVIEW: The party members contended that the cities' business license ordinances applied only to commercial, profit-making businesses, and did not govern the activities of their nonprofit political newspaper. The cities argued that the ordinances were valid, nondiscriminatory measures to raise revenue. In reversing the judgment entered in favor of the cities, the court held that the party members' newspaper was a noncommercial, nonprofit, purely political publication, and that the party members were exempt from the payment of the business license fees. The court observed that any person was exempt from taxation upon any act of distributing information or opinion of any kind, whether political, scientific, or religious in character, when done solely in an effort to spread knowledge and ideas, with no thought of commercial gain. The court found that the primary function of the newspaper was to present the views of the Socialist Party to the paper's subscribers and not to realize a pecuniary profit.


OUTCOME: The judgment that was entered in favor of the cities and against the party members was reversed. The court instructed the trial court to issue a permanent injunction restraining the cities and their agents and representatives from requiring the party members to secure and pay for a city business license as a condition for the distribution and sale of the party members' newspaper.

 

1226 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Atlantic Ins. Co. v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 23675


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


255 Cal. App. 2d 1; 62 Cal. Rptr. 784; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1233



October 5, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 30, 1967. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the City and County of San Francisco. H. A. van der Zee, Judge.

Action by fire and casualty insurance companies to recover retaliatory taxes levied by the State Board of Equalization.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Judgment for defendant modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) denying recovery of retaliatory taxes imposed pursuant to Cal. Ins. Code §685 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, who were Texas fire and casualty insurance companies, sought review of judgment denying recovery of retaliatory taxes. The levy had been made by respondent Board of Equalization, pursuant to Cal. Ins. Code § 685 et seq., upon determination that insurance tax laws of State of Texas discriminated against California-based insurance companies and hence, under California statute, called for retaliatory levy. On appeal the court affirmed the judgment as it determined Texas law discriminated against California insurers doing business in Texas and that burdens placed by Texas upon California insurers doing business in Texas were greater than burdens placed by California upon Texas insurers doing business in California. Appellants' contention that California statute violated commerce and equal protection clauses of U.S. Constitution was without merit because of the provisions of McCarran-Ferguson Act, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 1011-1015 and because the imposition of tax was condition precedent to admission to California.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because Texas law discriminated against California insurers doing business in Texas and burdens placed by Texas upon California insurers doing business in Texas were greater than burdens placed by California upon Texas insurers doing business in California; judgment was modified by augmenting schedule of recovery.

 

1227 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


United Farm Workers Organizing Committee v. Superior Court of Kern County


Civ. No. 858


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


254 Cal. App. 2d 768; 62 Cal. Rptr. 567; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1454; 66 L.R.R.M. 2514; 56 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P51,768



September 28, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Kern County from enjoining the exercise of the constitutional right of free speech by means of sound amplification in a labor dispute. Marvin Ferguson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner unions filed a proceeding in prohibition, which sought to restrain respondent Superior Court of Kern County from enjoining the exercise of free speech by means of sound amplification on the property owned by real party in interest employer.


OVERVIEW: A strike was ongoing against the employer and the unions were involved in picketing activities outside the employer's property. The employer brought an action against the unions, which sought a preliminary injunction. The Superior Court of Kern County granted the injunction, which included a provision that barred any speech disseminated through sound amplification. The court issued a peremptory writ of prohibition that directed the Superior Court of Kern County to refrain from enforcing the portion of the preliminary injunction that prohibited the use of bullhorns in connection with peaceful picketing during daylight working hours. An absolute prohibition of amplified speech was a violation of the rights granted by the First Amendment. The court held that the right to free speech embodied the means used for its dissemination because the right was worthless in the absence of a meaningful method of its expression. The dissemination of information concerning the facts of the labor dispute was regarded as being within the area of free discussion that was protected by the First Amendment. The court found that the use of a bullhorn could be reasonably restricted, but not totally banned.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of prohibition directing the Superior Court of Kern County to refrain from enforcing by contempt proceedings or otherwise that portion of the preliminary injunction that absolutely prohibited the union's reasonable use of bullhorns in connection with peaceful picketing during daylight working hours.

 

1228 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sommers v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 31070


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


254 Cal. App. 2d 605; 62 Cal. Rptr. 523; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1435



September 22, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 15, 1967. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Thomas C. Yager, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus by property owners against a city to require the issuance of a building permit for the remodeling of a gasoline service station.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which affirmed the decision by respondents, city and its administrative officials, to refuse the issuance of a building permit for the remodeling of a gasoline service station because the owners failed to comply with the demands under Los Angeles Municipal Code § 12.37. The owners then sought mandamus.


OVERVIEW: The property owners sought a building permit to remodel a gas station. The city denied the permit, claiming that the owners failed to comply with § 12.37 unless and until the owners dedicated an easement for public street purposes along the south and east ends of their property. The owners received a hearing on the issue where the southern easement was reduced by three feet but otherwise sustained. The owners claimed that the section was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to them. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of the city. The court held that § 12.37 was not unconstitutional on its face as it was a valid exercise of the city's police powers. The court also held that the requirements levied on the owners under § 12.37 were reasonably related to a public issue, namely increased traffic concerns and increased accessibility. Thus, the court held that the trial court was justified in concluding that the application to the owners of § 12.37 bore a substantial relationship to the accomplishment of a proper public purpose within the police power, and in such application it was not arbitrary, unreasonable, or otherwise unlawful as to them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the city's decision against the property owners and denied the writ of mandamus.

Johnson v. L. D. S. Trucking Co.


Civ. No. 23267


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


254 Cal. App. 2d 496; 62 Cal. Rptr. 501; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1421; 32 Cal. Comp. Cases 607



September 20, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco awarding attorney's fees to be paid from the proceeds of a workmen's compensation settlement. Joseph Karesh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) that awarded attorney's fees to plaintiff employee's attorney in an action based on a vehicle collision. The fees were to come from a portion of the settlement intended to reimburse the insurer for workmen's compensation benefits paid to the employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured in the course of his employment in a vehicle collision with a truck. The insurer was the employee's workmen's compensation carrier. The employee hired the attorney and obtained a settlement from a truck owner, and part of the judgment was to reimburse the insurer for benefits paid to the employee. The trial court entered a judgment that the attorney was entitled to attorney's fees from the insurer's share of the settlement, and the insurer sought review. The court reversed, holding that the settlement was not obtained solely through the efforts of the attorney; therefore the trial court was without authority to impose upon the insurer's share of the settlement an award of attorney's fees. Cal. Labor Code § 3860(c) did not apply; therefore its constitutionality was not determined.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that awarded attorney's fees to the employee's attorney.

Hom v. Chico Unified School Dist.


Civ. No. 11483


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


254 Cal. App. 2d 335; 61 Cal. Rptr. 920; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1399



September 14, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 13, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County and from an order sustaining a demurrer. J. F. Good, Judge.

Action for damages for personal injuries allegedly sustained while participating in high school physical education activities.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; purported appeal from order dismissed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer was sustained without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County (California), which sustained a demurrer filed by defendant school board in the minor's action for damages sustained while participating in high school physical education activities. The demurrer was based upon the minor's failure to comply with Cal. Gov't. Code § 911.2, 911.4, requiring timely claim filing as a prerequisite to suits against public agencies.


OVERVIEW: The minor was injured at school on October 8, 1964. On December 19, 1965, the minor filed an application for leave to present a late claim pursuant to Cal. Gov't. Code § 911.4 because the 100-day limitation of § 911.2 to present a claim had passed. The application alleged the minor's minority status as the sole ground of relief. When the school district denied the claim because the application was not filed within one year after the expiration of the 100-day period, the minor filed an action for damages. The school district demurred and the trial court sustained the demurrer. On appeal, the minor asserted that the claim filing statutes were unconstitutional as to minors. The court affirmed, holding that, if a minor filed an application for relief within the one-year extended period fixed by § 911.4, the relief was mandatory, making the claim filing conditions for minors more lenient. There were no arguments presented to establish the claim that the statutes were unconstitutional. In that the minor failed to file her claim within the extended period, the school board and the trial court were powerless to grant relief, and the demurrer was properly sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order sustaining the school district's demurrer and dismissing the action.

People v. Gray


Crim. No. 13513


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


254 Cal. App. 2d 256; 63 Cal. Rptr. 211; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1390



September 11, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 8, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment (orders granting probation) of the Municipal Court of Los Angeles Judicial District. Joan Dempsey Klein, Judge.

Prosecution for violating a municipal code relating to handbill posting upon a building.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from probation orders entered by the Municipal Court of Los Angeles Judicial District (California), which convicted them of violating a city ordinance that prohibited persons from posting signs on private property without the consent of the property owner.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that the trial court erred by placing upon them a heavier burden of proof than was required to prove a defense of discriminatory enforcement of the ordinance and that the court should review the evidence by an independent review to determine if they proved their defense. The State claimed that there was no such defense as discriminatory enforcement. The court determined that the trial court had instructed the jury that defendants were required to establish their defense based on an excessive burden and that defendants were only required to show by a preponderance of the evidence that the police had discriminated against them by enforcing the ordinance against them, but not others, who had also posted campaign signs on private property. The court also held that it was not inclined to do an independent review of the evidence, since it was reversing the orders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court.

Shakin v. Board of Medical Examiners


Civ. No. 30951


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


254 Cal. App. 2d 102; 62 Cal. Rptr. 274; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1371; 23 A.L.R.3d 1398



September 5, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 4, 1967, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 1, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. James G. Whyte, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Board of Medical Examiners to vacate and annul an order revoking a doctor's medical license to practice and to reinstate said license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor filed a proceeding in mandamus to compel defendant Board of Medical Examiners (board) to vacate and annul an order revoking his medical license and to reinstate the license. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denied the doctor's petition for a writ of mandate. The doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board charged the doctor with conviction of a state felony narcotics statute, using narcotics to the extent and in such manner as to be dangerous to himself and to the public, selling narcotics to an undercover officer as an alleged addict, and prescribing, furnishing, and administering morphine to himself. At a hearing in front of the board, the doctor was represented by counsel and did not raise the defense of entrapment. The doctor admitted that he was convicted of the felony, that he had self-prescribed morphine and Demerol, but that his personal use of drugs had ended, and that he sold narcotics to an addict outside the regular conduct of his profession and without making records of the sale. The court found that the board's hearing did not violate the Administrative Procedure Act, specifically, Cal. Gov't Code § 11517. The court further held that because the doctor did not bring up the affirmative defense of entrapment in the administrative hearing, he could not bring up the issue in the mandamus proceeding. The court also denied the doctor's motion to disqualify the judges of the court from hearing the appeal under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 170.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1233 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Goff v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 30962


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


254 Cal. App. 2d 45; 61 Cal. Rptr. 840; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 1366



August 31, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 25, 1967, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 25, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Otto J. Emme, Judge.

Action for damages resulting from an unsuccessful suicide attempt allegedly caused by the negligent release of a patient from a county hospital.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of nonsuit affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted a nonsuit in her action to recover damages from appellee county for the injuries she sustained when she unsuccessfully attempted to commit suicide.


OVERVIEW: The patient was under psychiatric care at the county hospital. Upon her release after treatment for depression, she attempted to commit suicide. As a result, the patient filed an action for damages resulting from an unsuccessful suicide attempt allegedly caused by her negligent release from the county hospital. The trial court nonsuited the action in favor of the county hospital. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that the hospital was immune from liability under Cal. Gov't. Code §§ 815.2, 854.8. The court found that there was nothing in the patient's opening statement that suggested that those in charge of the hospital unit in which she was being cared for entertained the erroneous idea that legally they could not be hosts any longer, and for that reason released her. The court concluded that the patient's opening statement did not disclose that she had a cause of action against the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of a nonsuit on the patient's action to recover for personal injuries she suffered when she tried to commit suicide in a hospital.

 

1234 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henze


Crim. No. 12310


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


253 Cal. App. 2d 986; 61 Cal. Rptr. 545; 1967 Cal. App. LEXIS 2432



August 29, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 25, 1967. McComb, J., Mosk, J., and Burke, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Max Z. Wisot, Judge.

Prosecution for burglary.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgments of conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) upon convictions for burglary. The issue for review was the validity of the detention, search, and arrest of defendants.


OVERVIEW: The police observed defendants from a distance. Defendants appeared to be counting coins and passing them back and forth. Defendants got into a vehicle, and the police followed them and pulled them over. Defendants were ordered to exit the vehicle. A bottle of red capsules was found in one defendant's pocket when he was searched. A further search of defendants and their vehicle revealed other property later identified as proceeds of a burglary. Defendants were charged and convicted of burglary. On appeal, the court reversed. There was not a sufficient basis to justify the temporary detention of defendants at the time that they were caught. The officers had no knowledge of the particular burglary, or any other reason to suspect defendants, either at the time of their original observations or at the time of the detention. The evidence obtained as a result of the detention was improperly obtained evidence and should have been excluded at trial. The court instructed the trial court that it was free to revoke or modify probation in one defendant's case if the situation so warranted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of conviction of burglary against defendants.
