1296 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Manchel v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 30082


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


245 Cal. App. 2d 501; 54 Cal. Rptr. 53; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1487



October 10, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 31, 1966, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 7, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred Gitelson, Judge.

Action for a declaration that a specified card game is not a game of chance and the playing of said game for money is not a violation of a county ordinance, and for an injunction restraining defendants from arresting or threatening to arrest, or enforcing the ordinance against, the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiffs reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county and police officers sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which permanently enjoined the county and the police officers from threatening to arrest or from arresting plaintiff card players for playing the card game panguingue for money.


OVERVIEW: The card players filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief that sought a determination as to whether the card game of panguingue was one of skill or chance. The county had an ordinance that imposed criminal sanctions upon persons that played certain card games within the county. The court reversed the injunction and held that the card players failed to allege throughout their pleadings any basis upon which the trial court could have granted an injunction. The card players did not allege that the ordinance was unconstitutional, or that the enforcement of the ordinance would have involved the invasion of property rights, which would have resulted in irreparable injury. The court determined that there was no property right and the threat of arrest under the circumstances was not a proper basis to have permitted the trial court to grant the injunctive relief. The court held that in the absence of a deprivation of a constitutional right or other essential facts, there was no basis to have allowed the trial court to grant declaratory relief or to have issued the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgment in favor of the card players and remanded the matter back to the trial court with directions to enter an order that dismissed the complaint.

 

1297 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Katcher v. Home Sav. & Loan Asso.


Civ. No. 28695


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


245 Cal. App. 2d 425; 53 Cal. Rptr. 923; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1481



October 6, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 21, 1966, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 30, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Charles A. Loring, Judge.

Action to enjoin defendant from use of its property to detriment of plaintiffs and their property and for damages caused by such use.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Summary judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners (owners) sought review of the grant of summary judgment by the Superior Court of Los Angeles (California) in favor of defendant bank in the owners' action that alleged the bank violated their acquired vested rights to a panoramic view from their homes that was violated when the bank provided financing for the construction of homes the owners' alleged violated the city's comprehensive zoning plan.


OVERVIEW: The owners contended that when they became owners of the air property their acquired a vested property right to a panoramic view overlooking a valley. The bank contended in its motion for summary judgment that everything done was completely authorized by permits issued pursuant to validly enacted city ordinances and building codes and that nothing which was done or maintained under express authority of a statute could have been deemed a nuisance under Cal. Civ. Code § 3482. The court affirmed finding that the owners failed to have provided any evidence in its answer to the motion for summary judgment, which raised any factual issue. The court held that it was long established that a landowner had no easement over adjoining land for light and air in the absence of an express grant or covenant. Further, the court concluded that all acts done by the bank were in accordance with applicable ordinances and zoning laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the bank in the owners' action alleging a violation of their vested rights to a panoramic view from their homes.

 

1298 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Sacramento City Unified School Dist.


Civ. No. 11249


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


245 Cal. App. 2d 278; 53 Cal. Rptr. 781; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1465



September 29, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 24, 1966, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 30, 1966. Peters, J., and Tobriner, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Murle C. Schreck, Judge.

Action to declare a rule prohibiting fraternities, sororities and secret clubs to be unconstitutional and to restrain a school district from enforcing such rule.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school district sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which declared a rule of the school district invalid as unconstitutional, and enjoined the school district from enforcing the rule, which prohibited the existence of certain "secret" organizations on high school campuses, in an action brought by plaintiff, a member of a club affected by the rule.


OVERVIEW: A member of a high school club sought to have a rule of the governing board of the school district declared invalid as unconstitutional. The trial court found for the member, declaring the rule "void as applied to the plaintiff." The school district and its agents were enjoined from enforcing it. The school district appealed. The court reversed the judgment, concluding that the clubs at issue were in fact "secret" as described by the legislature, meaning that membership was exclusive in those social clubs which, operating off-campus, nevertheless derived their membership wholly or in part from high schools, and clubs that practiced a process of selection to create a membership composed of the "socially elite" and which sought by such process to maintain that class segregation, by self-perpetuation, "rushing," "pledging," and admitting a limited number of new members. The court declared such clubs "secret" clubs as a matter of law, and found that rules prohibiting the clubs did not violate the First Amendment or the Fourteenth Amendment, or Cal. Const. art. I, § 11, providing that general laws shall have uniform operation, or any of the other provisions listed by the club member.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and directed the trial court to enter judgment for the school district, finding that the challenged rule was neither in excess of the powers delegated to the school board by the legislature, nor in violation of any constitutional right of the club member.

 

1299 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Marquez


Crim. No. 11842


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


245 Cal. App. 2d 253; 53 Cal. Rptr. 854; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1461



September 28, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 18, 1966, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 23, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Leroy Dawson and Joseph L. Call, Judges.

Prosecution for the illegal sale of heroin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the orders of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) which convicted him, after a bench trial, of the illegal sale of heroin. Pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 6451, the trial court found that defendant was addicted to heroin and made a commitment order. The Director of Corrections certified that defendant was not a fit subject for treatment. He was returned to the trial court, where a prison sentence was imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised the issue of the constitutionality of Cal. Penal Code § 6453, under which the Director of Corrections returned defendant to the trial court. He argued that the trial court erred in rejecting his challenge to the process. The court found no basis to rule that the § 6453 was unconstitutional. The statutory scheme provided screens for eligibility. A trial judge instituted commitment proceedings in cases where addiction was seen unless he found that a defendant was not a fit subject for commitment. The final decision of whether a defendant was likely to be helped by treatment was placed in the hands of experts in rehabilitation; it was not left to the determination of the trial judge. As a defendant had no absolute right to treatment under the program, continuance of treatment could properly be based on any reasonable criterion. The record showed that defendant was unwilling or unable to participate in the rehabilitation center programs. Finally, the evidence supported defendant's conviction because he had delivered heroin to an officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment of conviction against defendant.

 

1300 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Rogers


Civ. No. 30014


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


245 Cal. App. 2d 101; 53 Cal. Rptr. 572; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1450



September 21, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 16, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County determining that no inheritance tax is due and from a judgment establishing the fact of death. Donald R. Wright, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed appeal from judgment dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state controller (controller) sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 13672 (Code) was unconstitutional and that no inheritance tax was due from respondent taxpayer after the death of his spouse.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer moved from Ohio to California and thereafter purchased real property with funds earned in, and which were classified as separate property in Ohio. California law permitted a surviving joint tenant to avoid inheritance tax where the surviving spouse furnished the entire purchase price did not apply to the taxpayer's property because it was purchased with "quasi community property," rather than separate or community property under the Code. The superior court held that the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and various state constitutional provisions, and declared that no inheritance tax was due. The court reversed the judgment or the superior court, holding that the resulting distinction in the treatment of land purchased with California funds as opposed to Ohio funds was permissible because it was part of an overall scheme to assimilate the rights of a nonacquiring spouse in marital property acquired elsewhere with the rights of California domiciliaries, rather than a distinction based strictly upon the source of the taxpayer's funds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the superior court that determined that no inheritance tax was due and dismissed the controller's appeal of the superior court's judgment establishing the fact of the death of the taxpayer's spouse.

 

1301 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carter


Crim. No. 10995


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


245 Cal. App. 2d 48; 53 Cal. Rptr. 660; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1444



September 20, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. J. Howard Ziemann, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft from the person.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction on plea of guilty of simple assault affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant of simple assault after entry of defendant's guilty plea to that charge as a lesser included offense in the crime of grand theft from the person, which was the crime charged in the information. Defendant argued that she was never properly arraigned because simple assault was not necessarily included in the charged offense.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that simple assault was necessarily included in the grand theft crime charged in the information. On appeal, the court affirmed on other grounds. The record established that all parties had assumed that the assault was a lesser-included offense in the crime of grand theft. The purpose of an arraignment was to inform an accused of the charge and to give her an opportunity to plead to it or to move to set it aside. Defendant was properly arraigned on the grand theft charge and was given an opportunity to plead to that charge. Instead, defendant chose to plead guilty to assault because it was assumed to have been an included offense. Although the arraignment was technically flawed, a technical impropriety could be waived by acquiescence where no substantial impairment of rights occurred, and there was no evidence to indicate that defendant's rights were impaired by the acceptance of her plea. Consequently, the court held that defendant's guilty plea to simple assault constituted her admission that assault was included within the language of the information and that it amounted to a waiver of her right to complain about the procedural error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

1302 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Verner, Hilby & Dunn v. Monte Sereno


Civ. No. 22866


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


245 Cal. App. 2d 29; 53 Cal. Rptr. 592; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1441



September 20, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 20, 1966, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 16, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. O. Vincent Bruno, Judge.

Action seeking a declaration that a municipal ordinance regulating and licensing certain businesses, trades and professions is unconstitutional and for relief from payment of licensing fees.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for defendant city reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which upheld the constitutionality of defendant city's ordinance regulating and licensing certain businesses, trades, and professions.


OVERVIEW: The corporation brought a declaratory relief action against the city to obtain an adjudication of the unconstitutionality of Monte Sereno, Cal., Ordinance 16 dealing with the regulation and licensing of businesses, trades, and professions. The trial court upheld its constitutionality. On appeal, the court reversed with directions. The court held that Ordinance 16 was not a purely revenue measure, as found by the trial court. It attempted to regulate the professions of civil engineering and land surveying and it thereby infringed upon a field preempted by the state and created a conflict with the general law, in violation of Cal. Const. art. XI, § 11. Because the licensing portion of Ordinance 16 was an inseparable part of a regulatory scheme excluded by state laws applicable to engineers and surveyors, it was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which upheld the constitutionality of a the city ordinance regulating and licensing certain businesses, trades, and professions. The court remanded with directions.

 

1303 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bennett


Crim. No. 11403


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


245 Cal. App. 2d 10; 53 Cal. Rptr. 579; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1440



September 19, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County recommitting defendant to the Department of Mental Hygiene for placement in a state institution pursuant to Welf. & Inst. Code, §§ 5518, 5519. Harry V. Peetris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) which recommitted defendant to the Department of Mental Hygiene for placement in a state institution pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 5518 and 5519 as a mentally disordered sex offender. Defendant contended that the hearing resulting in his recommitment was not held in accordance with applicable sections of the California Welfare and Institutions Code.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with battery, disturbing the peace, and making annoying telephone calls. Defendant entered a plea of nolo contendere but, before sentencing, the proceeding was suspended and defendant transferred to the trial court for proceedings to determine whether he was a mentally disordered sex offender. Defendant was admitted to the state hospital for a 90-day examination period and was subsequently committed thereto for an indefinite period. Six months later, defendant requested that the superintendent of the hospital file a report pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5519. The report indicated that defendant was still a danger to society but that he had received maximum hospital benefits. The report recommended that defendant be committed to other facilities of the department for an indeterminate period. The court held that the trial court erred in concluding that it could not appoint independent psychiatrists to examine defendant because, in a recommitment hearing granted under § 5519, it was mandatory that such doctors be appointed. The court concluded that defendant had the right to be represented by counsel, present witnesses, and cross-examine witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court.

 

1304 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. Nos. 631, 632, 633


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


244 Cal. App. 2d 843; 53 Cal. Rptr. 597; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1635



September 15, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 13, 1966, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 9, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Jay L. Henry, Judge.

Consolidated actions for refunds of income taxes paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers, who were partners, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which affirmed the determination of respondent state tax board that assessed a deficiency against the taxpayers on the grounds that neither the partnership returns nor the taxpayers' individual returns reported their total gross income as required by Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 17297.


OVERVIEW: The partnership supplied amusement devices, including "Bingo" pinball machines and other types of pinball machines to location owners. The owners made payouts for free games won on the "Bingo" pinball machines, which were gambling devices. The partnership reimbursed the owners for the payouts. Expenses were paid out of the gross income of the machines, and the owners and partnership split the remaining income. The partnership paid income tax on its net income. The board determined that the partnership was not entitled to deduct its expenses and assessed a deficiency for the entire amount of the machines' income, including the nongambling machines. On appeal, the State Board of Equalization affirmed the assessment but modified it downwards because the partnership was involved in joint ventures with the owners, who were responsible for half the income tax. The modified assessment was affirmed on judicial review and the taxpayers paid it. On appeal, the court affirmed that the partnership was not entitled to deductions for its illegal gambling activities under Cal. Penal Code § 330b. Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 17297 was not unconstitutional as a fiscal measure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the assessment of income tax deficiencies by the board against the taxpayers.

 

1305 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. McGennis


Crim. No. 12368


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


244 Cal. App. 2d 527; 53 Cal. Rptr. 215; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1603



August 30, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from judgments of the Municipal Court of the Los Angeles Judicial District. George M. Dell, Judge.

Prosecution for violating Los Angeles Municipal Code provisions relating to gambling.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgments of dismissal reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from judgments of the Municipal Court of the Los Angeles Judicial District (California), which dismissed the complaints against defendants for violating §§ 43.13.1 and 43.13.2 of the Los Angeles Municipal Code for gambling.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with gambling, and the trial court dismissed the complaints against them. The state appealed, and the court reversed and remanded with directions to deny the motions to dismiss concluding that §§ 43.13.1 and 43.13.2 had not been preempted by the state to the extent that the sections were constitutionally invalid. The court concluded that §§ 43.13.1 and 43.13.2 were a valid exercise of the local police power. The court found that the general laws of the state did not forbid as criminal the conduct forbidden by the sections because if the legislature had intended to regulate such conduct, it would have done so. The court concluded that the state had not occupied the field of gambling or gaming to the extent that the two sections were in conflict with the general laws. The court held that the sections were no more than a regulation of a municipal affair, and not exclusively a matter of statewide concern.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the complaints against defendants for gambling.

 

1306 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Paul v. Eggman


Civ. No. 566


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


244 Cal. App. 2d 461; 53 Cal. Rptr. 237; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1595



August 23, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 19, 1966. Mosk, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Tulare County granting a preliminary injunction to prohibit an orange grower from transporting his produce to another county and selling it to the public in violation of the Fruit, Nut and Vegetable Standards Act. John Locke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant orange grower sought review of an order of the Superior Court, Tulare County (California), which granted a preliminary injunction requested by respondent, the director of agriculture, prohibiting the grower from transporting his produce to another county and selling it to the public, in violation of the Fruit, Nut, and Vegetable Standards Act, Cal. Agric. Code §§ 784, 796.2.


OVERVIEW: The grower owned an orange grove in Tulare county. For the past 10 years, he personally sold oranges from a location in Santa Clara County. The oranges were stored in open field containers and sold in varying quantities. The director of agriculture filed suit against the grower for civil penalties and injunctive relief for violations of Cal. Agric. Code §§ 784, 796.2, which imposed requirements for standardized packaging and size of fruit. The statute allowed an exemption for a grower who sold fruit near the point of production so long as the selling location was within the county where the fruit was grown. After a hearing, the trial court granted a preliminary injunction against the grower. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: 1) the grower was not a "retailer" within the meaning of the statutes as that term applied to one who bought fruit for resale and had previously met standardization requirements; 2) statutory enactments relative to standard containers for foodstuffs were a valid exercise of the police power; and 3) the county line limitation was reasonably related to preventing harmful intrastate marketing practices.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court granting a preliminary injunction against the grower.

 

1307 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Alexander


Crim. No. 278


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


244 Cal. App. 2d 301; 53 Cal. Rptr. 65; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1574



August 17, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 14, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Albert H. Mundt, Judge.

Prosecution for maliciously interfering with gas main and for burglary of gas well pumping station with intent to commit theft.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction of second degree burglary affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) that convicted him of maliciously interfering with a gas meter in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 593c and burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted following a bench trial of maliciously interfering with a gas meter and burglary after he and his girlfriend broke into a building housing a gas well meter and removed mercury therefrom. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. Under Cal. Penal Code § 459, every person who entered any mine with intent to commit larceny was guilty of burglary. The building housing the gas well was included in the definition of "mine" at Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 2200. Further, removal of mercury from the recorder in the gas well meter was interference with the flow of gas under Cal. Penal Code § 593c.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1308 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hardeman


Crim. No. 5181


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


244 Cal. App. 2d 1; 53 Cal. Rptr. 168; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1543



August 4, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 2, 1966, and the Opinion and Judgment were Modified to Read as Printed Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 23, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment (order granting probation) of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County and from orders denying motions for new trial and arrest of judgment. Folger Emerson, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to pervert and obstruct justice and the due administration of the law and for conspiracy to commit arson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; appeal from orders dismissed. Judgment of conviction reversed as to arson charge and affirmed as to other charge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) that granted him probation but also denied his motions for new trial and arrest of judgment relative to his convictions for conspiracy to obstruct justice and for conspiracy to commit arson. On appeal, he contended that the trial court made several incorrect evidentiary and procedural rulings and erred in giving certain instructions to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury for conspiracy to pervert and obstruct justice and of conspiracy to commit arson. Thereafter, the trial court entered an order that granted defendant probation and that denied defendant's motion for arrest of judgment and motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court summarily dismissed defendant's purported appeals from the denial of the motion for new trial and motion in arrest of judgment. Additionally, the court held that: (1) any error, if any, made by the trial court in overruling the demurrer to the obstruction of justice charge was not prejudicial; (2) the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction on both charges and that there was no prejudicial error in the rulings on the admission of evidence; (3) the trial court erred in giving the special instructions that it provided in response to queries from the jury on the arson charge, and that error prejudiced defendant so as to require reversal; and (4) the alleged misconduct of prosecution did not constitute reversible error. Thus, the trial court's order was affirmed as to the conspiracy to obstruct justice charge, but reversed as to the arson conspiracy charge.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order that granted defendant probation was affirmed insofar as it rested upon defendant's conviction for conspiracy to pervert and obstruct justice, and reversed as to the conviction for conspiracy to commit arson. The trial court erred in special instructions that it provided in answer to the jury's inquiries on the arson count, and that error was prejudicial and required reversal of defendant's conviction on that charge.

Estate of Preston


Civ. No. 8286


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


243 Cal. App. 2d 803; 52 Cal. Rptr. 790; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1736



August 2, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 15, 1966, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 28, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Lester Van Tatenhove, Judge.

Action to compel the guardian of an estate to file an account current and to pay for the care, support and maintenance of a patient in a state institution.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for petitioner affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) which compelled the guardian of an estate to pay the costs of the care, support and maintenance of a patient in a state institution to respondent state department of mental hygiene (department). The mentally retarded ward was committed, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 5258, to the department upon application of her parents at the age of 19.


OVERVIEW: The department sought payment for the costs of care, support, and maintenance of the patient from the patient's estate. The court affirmed the award to the department of the care, support, and maintenance costs of the guardian's ward. The court held that § 7011.5, Welfare and Institutions Code, which provided for recovery from the ward or his estate for costs incurred by the department, was constitutional. The court held that the committing judge used the discretionary power given to him to allow for the care of the ward by the department. The court held that had the judge not committed the ward, the guardian of the estate would have had the continuing duty to provide and care for the ward out of assets of her estate at home or in a private institution. The court found no law that constitutionally proscribed repayment by a mentally retarded person's estate for her care and maintenance while in a state institution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award to the department of the care, support, and maintenance costs of the guardian's ward.

People ex rel. Department of Public Works v. Rodoni


Civ. No. 561


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


243 Cal. App. 2d 771; 52 Cal. Rptr. 857; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1732



August 1, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order (denominated interlocutory judgment) of the Superior Court of Merced County determining that condemnation of certain real property was not for a public use and that the complaint be dismissed insofar as it purported to condemn such real property. Gregory P. Maushart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed on motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of public works challenged an order of the Superior Court of Merced County (California) that determined that the department's condemnation of certain real property of respondent property owners was not for a public use. The department's complaint was dismissed insofar as it purported to condemn the real property at issue.


OVERVIEW: The department attempted to condemn a parcel of property pursuant to Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 104.1, which permitted the condemnation of the remainder of a parcel if the remainder would be of little value to the owner after condemnation of the portion of the parcel for state highway purposes. The department's condemnation of portions of two small parcels left a third parcel, comprised of 54 acres, completely landlocked. The property owners challenged the action, claiming that the department's attempt to condemn the largest parcel was not for a public use. They claimed that § 104.1 was unconstitutional. The trial court entered an interlocutory judgment, finding that the taking was not for public use and ordering that condemnation of the smaller parcels proceed to trial along with severance damages for the largest parcel. On appeal, the court held that the judgment was a nonappealable interlocutory judgment. It would have addressed the constitutional question, but it had not been presented with an appropriate writ of prohibition or of mandate. It could not construe the department's appeal as a petition for a writ because the trial court was not a party to the action before the court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

County of Alameda v. Espinoza


Civ. No. 23549


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One

Action by a county against a minor's parent to recover the cost of care, support and maintenance of the minor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal, following the sustaining of a demurrer without leave to amend, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the judgment of the Municipal Court of the Oakland-Piedmont Judicial District of Alameda County (California), which sustained respondent father's demurrer in the county's action against the father to recover the cost of care, support, and maintenance of a minor. The case was transferred from the appellate department of the superior court.


OVERVIEW: The county brought an action against the father to recover the cost of care, support, and maintenance of a minor child. 1312 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Spindler Realty Corp. v. Monning


Civ. No. 29616


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


243 Cal. App. 2d 255; 53 Cal. Rptr. 7; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1672



June 29, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 27, 1966, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 24, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying motions to vacate and set aside the judgment and to enter new and different judgments. Otto M. Kaus, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus or certiorari to compel issuance of a building permit and to rescind the action denying the permit, consolidated with an action to enjoin enforcement of a certain zoning ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; appeals from orders dismissed. Judgments for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant realty corporation challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which, in a consolidated action against appellees, the City of Los Angeles and a city official, entered judgments and orders denying motions to vacate and to set aside the judgment, denying a petition for a writ of mandate and denying an injunction.


OVERVIEW: The realty corporation sought a writ of mandate or writ of certiorari commanding the city official to issue a building permit for which it had applied and to rescind his action denying the permit. The realty corporation also sought an injunction against the enforcement of a certain zoning ordinance and a judgment that the ordinance was null and void insofar as it affected its property. The trial court denied the relief sought by the realty corporation and the court affirmed. The court held that the realty corporation did not have a vested right to build where it had not yet obtained a building permit. The City of Los Angeles was not estopped from enforcing an ordinance to zone the realty corporation's property in a manner inconsistent with the realty corporation's plans. The court rejected the realty corporation's argument that it had a nonconforming use protected by § 21.23C of the Los Angeles Municipal Code. The court held that the activity of the realty corporation at the time it became subject to a zoning ordinance, and not its plans regarding the future use of that property, determined the scope of the nonconforming use excepted from the restrictions imposed by the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the realty corporation and in favor of the City of Los Angeles and the city official.

 

1313 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Municipal Court for Southern Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 23132


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


243 Cal. App. 2d 55; 52 Cal. Rptr. 189; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1645



June 22, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 17, 1966. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Edmund Scott, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain a municipal court from proceeding in a criminal case.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), denying his petition for an alternative and permanent writ of prohibition in which he argued, as he did in his demurrer, that the State's complaint charging him with seven violations of Cal. Penal Code § 146c and seven violations of Cal. Bus. and Prof. Code § 17500, was based on statutes that were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Abandoning his challenge of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17500, defendant argued on appeal that Cal. Penal Code § 146c failed to meet the requirements of due process because its language, in proscribing the designation of any organization that included "peace officer, police, or law enforcement" in its name unless 90 percent or more of the members fit the categories, was vague and indefinite. The statute further prohibited the solicitation of members to such organization. On appeal, defendant argued that the statutory language failed to provide a sufficiently explicit standard for persons subject thereto and that the mere act of "designating" was not, under any circumstances, a crime. In rejecting defendant's arguments, the court held that the subject phrase provided adequate warning of the conduct proscribed and furnished a sufficiently distinct standard for the administration of § 146c. Moreover, defendant used a specific name example that § 146c barred in soliciting others to subscribe to a publication. Further, defendant was foreclosed from challenging the designation portion of the statute because he lacked standing to do so as he was charged with the solicitation portion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1314 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tuttle


Crim. No. 2402


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


242 Cal. App. 2d 883; 52 Cal. Rptr. 204; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1200



June 20, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County denying a motion to release to defendant certain property used as an exhibit in a forgery prosecution. Robert W. Conyers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed on motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied defendant's motion to release to him certain property used as an exhibit in a forgery prosecution and other property retained by the police that was not introduced into evidence. Defendant filed the motion after his conviction for forgery became final. The People filed a motion to dismiss defendant's appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant forged the signature of a payor on checks, cashed them, received money from the persons cashing the checks, and was convicted of forgery. Upon defendant's arrest, the police removed cash from defendant and took possession of items of personal property. Some of the property, including money, was admitted into evidence at trial as exhibits, and the police retained the property that was not admitted. Defendant argued that he was permitted to appeal the order under Cal. Penal Code § 1237(3) because it affected his substantial rights. In dismissing the appeal, the court held that defendant had mistaken his remedy. Defendant sought the return of the exhibits under Cal. Penal Code § 1418, which was permissive in nature and did not confer upon defendant a right to obtain release of the exhibits. The order did not affect any substantial right that was a part of the criminal action because the order did not involve the forgery charge against defendant or his rights as affected by the charge. Further, the return of the property not admitted into evidence was wholly without statutory authorization. Thus, the order was not appealable under Cal. Penal Code § 1237(3).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal.

 

1315 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. La Farge


Civ. No. 22065


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


242 Cal. App. 2d 806; 51 Cal. Rptr. 877; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1188



June 15, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 15, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Lyle E. Cook, Judge.

Action to recover for breach of a written contract.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment awarding allegedly inadequate damages affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employment agent sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which awarded the agent only $ 13 in his action against respondent job seeker for breach of a written contract.


OVERVIEW: The job seeker sought assistance from the agent to find employment. The parties entered into a written agreement, which required the job seeker to pay the agent $ 120 for information by which he could secure a bona fide employment interview. The job seeker obtained such an interview and was hired, but the employment lasted only 10 days. The agent brought the matter before the labor commissioner, who determined that the job seeker should pay a fee of $ 13. The agent then filed an action seeking a trial de novo. The trial court awarded the agent $ 13, and the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the written agreement was illegal, and it could not support an award for damages for its breach. The court found that the contract violated the provisions of the Labor Code relating to private employment agencies and contravened the intention of the legislature in enacting statutes for the protection of job-seeking workers. The court held that the contractual scheme resembled a registration fee prohibited by Cal. Lab. Code § 1633. The court found that $ 13 was the reasonable value of the agent's services.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which awarded the agent only $ 13 in his action against the job seeker for breach of a written contract.

 

1316 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Davis


Crim. No. 11822


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


242 Cal. App. 2d 645; 51 Cal. Rptr. 702; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1168



June 3, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 24, 1966, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 27, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody on the ground that a portion of the misdemeanor statute under which petitioners were convicted was unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, challenging the judgment of a superior court (California), which convicted them under Cal. Penal Code § 650 1/2 of willfully and wrongfully committing any act which openly outraged public decency.


OVERVIEW: Defendants sought release from custody on the ground that the portion of Cal. Penal Code § 650 1/2 under which they were convicted was unconstitutional. The court granted the petition, found the statute unconstitutionally vague, and set aside the convictions. The court held that the terms of a penal statute creating a new offense were required to be sufficiently explicit to inform those who were subject to it what conduct on their part could render them liable to its penalties. A statute that either forbade or required the doing of an act in terms so vague that men of common intelligence had to guess at its meaning, and differed as to its application, violated the first essential of due process of law. The court examined various aids to legislative construction and was unable to determine the meaning of public decency as used in § 650 1/2.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ, set aside defendants' convictions, and discharged them from all restraints, actual, constructive, or threatened. The court held that the statute under which defendants were convicted was unconstitutionally vague.

 

1317 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Southern Pacific Co. v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 29462


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


242 Cal. App. 2d 38; 51 Cal. Rptr. 197; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1096



May 6, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 27, 1966, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 29, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Bernard S. Jefferson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the issuance of a permit to build a warehouse.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner railroad sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied the railroad's claim against respondent city that a zoning ordinance was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to the railroad's mandamus action to compel the issuance of a permit.


OVERVIEW: The railroad, as the owner of property abutting on South Alameda Street in Los Angeles, applied for a permit to build a warehouse thereon. When the city refused to issue such permit unless there was compliance with § 12.37 of the Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code, requiring the railroad to dedicate a portion of its property to the city for street widening purposes in accordance with its master plan of community development, the railroad brought a mandamus proceeding to compel the issuance of such permit. The trial court found against the railroad on its claims that § 12.37 was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to the facts at bar. The railroad appealed. The court affirmed, holding that a city could require the dedication of land for the widening of an existing street as a condition to its approval of a subdivision map, and such a condition, where reasonably related to the increased traffic and other needs of the proposed subdivision, did not constitute a taking of private property without compensation. The court held that the ordinance's requirement for judgment on the part of the administrative officer was not so vague as to be constitutionally objectionable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city in the railroad's mandamus action to compel the issuance of a permit.

 

1318 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Huss


Crim. No. 9930


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


241 Cal. App. 2d 361; 51 Cal. Rptr. 56; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1250



April 5, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 28, 1966. Roth, P. J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted. Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 1, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Herbert V. Walker, Judge.

Prosecutions for assault, assault with force likely to produce great bodily injury, and for conspiracy to commit forcible assault, forcible assault on a police officer, assault, battery, and riot.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgments of conviction reversed as to conspiracy count and affirmed in all other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Five members of the American Nazi Party, wearing party uniforms, steel helmets, and swastika armbands, picketed a meeting held to celebrate the fifteenth anniversary of the independence of Israel. Public disorder resulted, and all five were convicted and sentenced on charges of conspiracy and assault by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California). Three defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the jury instructions defined disturbing the peace to include acts tending to provoke others to disturb the peace and that consequently the jury was given the erroneous impression that it could consider defendants' use of provocative slogans, symbols, and costumes as evidence of a conspiracy to riot. The court reversed the conspiracy convictions but affirmed the assault convictions. Under the First Amendment, it could not be made an offense merely to invite dispute or to bring about a condition of unrest. Moreover, California did not recognize the doctrine that fighting words or insulting language justified an assault. Thus, the court concluded that the instructions unconstitutionally invaded the domain of free speech by suggesting to the jury that it could infer a conspiracy to riot from defendants' display of provocative signs and slogans which could incite others to break the peace. The jury was not told that those picketed had no right to break the peace or resort to violence. Finally, assaults committed in the course of picketing or of public demonstrations could, as here, be promptly and severely punished under the California Penal Code.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of conviction for all defendants as to the conspiracy count but affirmed the judgments of conviction as to the assault counts.

Cummings v. California State Teachers' Retirement Board


Civ. No. 22524


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


241 Cal. App. 2d 149; 50 Cal. Rptr. 391; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1226



March 28, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Edward Molkenbuhr, Judge.

Action by a teacher to have her pension payments computed according to the statutes in effect in 1955 when she started teaching, and to have certain 1957 amendments to the Education Code declared unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which found in favor of defendant, the California State Teachers' Retirement Board, in the teacher's action to have certain 1957 amendments to the Education Code declared unconstitutional and to have her pension payments computed pursuant to the statutes in effect in 1955.


OVERVIEW: The teacher contended that certain 1957 amendments to the Education Code, set forth in 1957 Cal. Stat. 2118, p. 3751, were unconstitutional as applied to her because they reduced her pension as it should have been computed under the law in effect on July 1, 1956. On appeal, she asserted that the Board's and the trial court's computation resulted in a reduction from the allowance to which she became entitled by engaging in employment under the provisions of the 1955 amendments to the Education Code, set forth in 1955 Cal. Stat. 1395, p. 2491. The court held that the Board and trial court did not err in construing the applicable statutory provisions. The court found that the construction of the statutes sought by the teacher, the majority of whose service was part-time, would have given her a windfall as compared with full-time employees. The court reasoned that under the teacher's construction, a lifetime full-time teacher and a former part-time teacher who both had the same "final compensation" at the time of eligibility for retirement would have received the same allowance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

People v. Davis


Crim. No. 10614


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


241 Cal. App. 2d 51; 50 Cal. Rptr. 215; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1211



March 22, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a motion for a new trial. William E. Fox, Judge.

Prosecution for first degree robbery, attempted robbery and assault with a deadly weapon.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified and affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment of conviction modified to vacate sentence on one count of assault, in all other respects affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), defendant was convicted of first degree robbery, attempted robbery, and two counts of assault with a deadly weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two witnesses identified defendant as a participants in a robbery. Subsequently, three witnesses identified defendant as a participants in an attempted robbery, which also involved two assaults. At trial, defendant provided alibi testimony. For the first robbery, defendant's wife testified that he was home. For the second incident, defendant's sister and mother testified that defendant was with them. A police officer testified that defendant had made statements about playing pool during the first robbery. Defendant was convicted, and the trial court imposed concurrent sentences on the robbery, attempted robbery, and one assault charge, and imposed a consecutive sentence on the second assault conviction. The court held that the testimony of several witnesses was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction of the charges. The court determined that the officer's testimony was admissible for the limited purpose of showing prior inconsistent statements by defendant. The court found that one of the assault convictions had to be vacated because attempted robbery required one act of violence and the separate conviction resulted in multiple punishment for the same offense.


OUTCOME: The court modified the sentence imposed on defendant, vacating the sentence for one count of assault, and it affirmed defendant's conviction.

Hopkins v. Contractors' State License Board


Civ. No. 7551


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


240 Cal. App. 2d 710; 49 Cal. Rptr. 917; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1402



March 11, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County. Hilton H. McCabe, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Contractors' State License Board to vacate and set aside a decision revoking a contractor's license.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment granting writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Contractors' State License Board challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which commanded the Board to vacate and set aside its decision revoking the contractor's licenses of respondents, contractor and employee.


OVERVIEW: The contractor held a license and furnished the qualifying experience for the employee. After the contractor was adjudged bankrupt, an accusation was filed charging him with a violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 7113.5. His bankruptcy schedules established that a substantial portion of the liabilities from which the contractor sought to be discharged represented amounts owed for labor, supplies, and materials furnished for his use as a licensed contractor. The Board revoked the contractor's license and, without benefit of the contractor's qualifying experience, the employee's license was also revoked. The lower court vacated the order revoking the licenses and the court reversed. It rejected respondents' contentions that § 7113.5 was unconstitutional because it discriminated against contractors who resorted to bankruptcy. Instead, the court held that the statute was a valid exercise of the police power where the bankruptcy related to the licensee's business as a contractor. Further, the legislature had laid down definite standards for administrative implementation of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which ordered the Board to vacate its order revoking respondents' licenses, and instructed that a judgment be entered denying the writ.

Loop v. State


Civ. No. 22492


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


240 Cal. App. 2d 591; 49 Cal. Rptr. 909; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1388



March 7, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Napa County. William L. Blanckenburg, Judge.

Action for the wrongful death of a paying patient in a state hospital.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer was sustained without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the mother of a patient who died in a state hospital and others similarly situated (the class), brought a wrongful death action against defendant state and others. The Superior Court of Napa County (California) sustained the state's demurrer without leave to amend, and dismissed the case against the state. The class appealed.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that a mental patient was fatally injured when a fellow patient struck him, causing the mental patient to strike his head on a concrete wall. The court noted that the action arose during the interim period between the rendering of a decision, which allowed such wrongful death suits against the state to go forward, and the imposition of a moratorium by the legislature, during which time the legislature proposed to study the problems created by the decision and to enact appropriate legislation on the subject. The court further noted that two years later, the legislature enacted 1963 Cal. Stat. 1681, § 1, codified at Cal. Gov't Code § 854.8, which provided that the state was immune from suits for damages to mental patients proximately caused by fellow patients. 1963 Cal. Stat. 1681, § 45, subd. (a), declared that the act had retroactive application. The trial court determined that Cal. Gov't Code § 854.8 applied during the interim period after the decision was rendered and before the moratorium was imposed, and, therefore, the state was immune from liability in the instant action. The court agreed, and affirmed the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which dismissed the wrongful death action as against the state.

 

1323 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Potter


Crim. No. 2139


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


240 Cal. App. 2d 621; 49 Cal. Rptr. 892; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1392



March 7, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 28, 1966, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 4, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Charles A. Bauer, Judge.

Prosecution for wiretapping and criminal conspiracy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which convicted them of wiretapping and of conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged their convictions for wiretapping and conspiracy on the grounds that California's wiretapping statute was unconstitutional as an ex post facto statute and that Congress had preempted the field of electronic communications. On appeal, the court held that the federal wiretapping statute applied to intrastate as well as interstate communications. However, a state prohibition against wiretapping within its own borders did not conflict with the Supremacy Clause contained in the United States Constitution because the Federal Communications Act did not evince a congressional plan to occupy the field of wiretapping. The court also held that the wiretapping statute was not unconstitutional as an ex post facto statute because the statute was effective many years prior to the filing of the charges involved and the punishment described was not in any way changed after commission of the offenses involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendants of the crimes of wiretapping and conspiracy.

Phillips v. Board of Police Comm'rs


Civ. No. 29008


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


240 Cal. App. 2d 410; 49 Cal. Rptr. 490; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1361



February 24, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Harold F. Collins, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel issuance of a permit to conduct a teenage dance and declaratory relief action seeking to have a municipal code section declared unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting writ reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of police commissioners sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted petitioner private sponsor's petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus to compel the board to issue a permit to conduct a teenage dance and declared that Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code, Ordinance No. 111348, § 103.118(a)(1), (2) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The sponsor applied for a permit under § 103.118 to hold a teenage dance, and a hearing examiner recommended that the permit be denied because of the sponsor's inability to provide adequate supervision. The board denied the permit, and the sponsor sought declaratory relief challenging the constitutionality of § 103.118 and a writ of mandate to compel the issuance of the permit. The trial court held that, although the purpose of the ordinance was to promote the welfare of teenagers, the classification permitting only nonprofit organizations to carry out that purpose was not reasonably related to the purpose of the ordinance. The court reversed, holding that § 103.118 was constitutionally valid because there was a substantial basis for the city council's conclusion that a nonprofit organization could better promote the objectives and purposes of the ordinance than one that was operated for profit. There was a constitutional, natural, and intrinsic distinction between profitmaking and nonprofit organizations as sponsors of teenage dances, and the distinction bore a substantial relationship to the main objective and purpose of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and vacated the peremptory writ of mandate.

In re Bacon


Civ. Nos. 22751, 22752, 22753, 22933


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


240 Cal. App. 2d 34; 49 Cal. Rptr. 322; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1313



February 8, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 2, 1966, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 5, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the Superior Court of Alameda County in session as a Juvenile Court, placing several minors on probation without wardship, applying certain rules of conduct and behavior to them, requiring them to report to the probation officer and requiring them to spend four weekends at the probation department's training academy. Robert H. Kroninger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juveniles challenged the decision of the Superior Court for Alameda County (California), which placed them on probation without wardship, applied certain rules of conduct and behavior to them, required them to report to the probation officer, and required them to spend four weekends at the probation department's training academy.


OVERVIEW: Juveniles contended that the probation department abused its discretion in commencing proceedings against them, the evidence was insufficient to sustain the finding of the trial court, and that their right to counsel was rendered ineffective. The court concluded that the probation department could commence proceedings against juveniles without making a preliminary investigation. The court held that there was nothing in the record to indicate that juveniles' representation by their counsel was impinged upon so as to result in a deprivation of rights violative of due process. The court further held that there was sufficient evidence to support the convictions since appellants committed the acts proscribed in the presence of Berkeley police officers. Finally, the court held that it could not say as a matter of law that the trial court abused its broad discretion in imposing the condition of probation since the court could not say that all reasonable minds would conclude that the subject condition was disproportionate to the offenses committed by appellants in view of the conclusion reached by the court that the evidence was sufficient to sustain a violation of the statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which determined that juveniles committed trespass and resisted arrest and imposed conditions on their probation.

People v. Stewart


Crim. No. 9764


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


240 Cal. App. 2d 1; 50 Cal. Rptr. 26; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1309



February 7, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 5, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Joseph A. Wapner, Judge.

Prosecution for robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction of second degree robbery affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant and a codefendant were convicted of robbery in the second degree. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denied defendant probation and sentenced him to state prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant came up behind the victim and grabbed him around his neck. The codefendant removed the victim's wallet and money from his pants pocket and ran. Defendant then let go and he ran. The victim identified defendant and the codefendant in a police lineup the next day. Defendant argued on appeal that he was denied his right to counsel of his own choosing, and the right to represent himself. The court disagreed and affirmed defendant's second-degree robbery conviction. After the jury was selected and sworn to try the cause, defendant requested another lawyer. After the trial court discussed the situation with defendant, defendant stated that he might as well represent himself. Upon further questioning the trial court determined that the defendant was incapable of representing himself. Thereafter, defendant indicated his desire to be represented by the public defender that was appointed to him. The court stated that in the absence of an intelligent and competent waiver of counsel, the trial court was justified in denying the defendant's demand to discharge his attorney. And, defendant was not prejudiced by the public defender's representation of him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for second degree robbery.

 

1328 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schaletzke


Crim. No. 10441


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


239 Cal. App. 2d 881; 49 Cal. Rptr. 275; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1831



February 3, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 30, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Herbert V. Walker, Judge.

Prosecution for committing a sex offense against a child.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) sentenced defendant to state prison after he pled guilty to a sexual offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court did not fulfill its duty when it sentenced the defendant to state prison instead of committing him to the state hospital and that commitment to prison without treatment, when he was a mentally disordered sex offender, inflicted cruel and unusual punishment. The court affirmed defendant's sentence, holding that the law afforded him no right to demand hospitalization as an alternative to a prison sentence when he was convicted of a felony. The trial court followed the requirements in Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 5512 and 5518 that the proceedings against defendant be adjourned pending a determination whether he was a mentally disordered sex offender. Following the recommendation of doctors, defendant was sent to a mental hospital for diagnosis. The hospital reported the defendant was not amenable to treatment and should be punished by the court. The trial court did institute sexual psychopathy proceedings but it did not have a duty to commit defendant to a hospital.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

McClatchey v. Rudd


Civ. No. 7663


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


239 Cal. App. 2d 605; 48 Cal. Rptr. 783; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1801



January 25, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 22, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Vincent A. Whelan, Judge.

Action to set aside an allegedly unlawful sale of estate property under a deed of trust.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to second amended complaint was sustained with leave to amend and plaintiff failed or refused to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrator sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which entered judgment in favor of defendants, the beneficiary and the trustee under the deed of trust, in the administrator's action to set aside an allegedly unlawful sale of estate property under a deed of trust.


OVERVIEW: The administrator brought an action against defendants seeking to set aside an allegedly unlawful sale of estate property under a deed of trust. The property in question had been owned by the administrator's decedent. It had been used as security on a loan from the beneficiary to the decedent. The property was foreclosed upon after the decedent's death. The lower court entered judgment in favor of defendants. Upon appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the administrator failed to protect the interests of the estate with regard to the property. The court found that the administrator not only failed to record a request for notice within the several months after being appointed administrator but, so far as the record showed, he also failed to supply the trustee or beneficiary with a new address after giving up the deceased's post office box. The court failed to find active fraud on the part of defendants or any concealment of the foreclosure proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of defendants.

Noonan v. Rousselot


Civ. No. 28139


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


239 Cal. App. 2d 447; 48 Cal. Rptr. 817; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1780



January 19, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 16, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. William E. Fox, Judge.

Action for damages for libel and conspiracy to deprive plaintiff of a fair election.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to third amended complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, California, which sustained defendant opponent's demurrer to the candidate's third amended complaint in the candidate's action for damages for libel and conspiracy to deprive the candidate of a fair election.


OVERVIEW: The candidate alleged that, when he qualified to run against his opponent, the opponent and others conspired to cause his defeat and to cause the opponent's nomination at the primary election by publishing a "tabloid" in newspaper format alleging in effect that the candidate was not a bona fide Republican, that he was entered in the campaign by the "collectivists and left wing democrats" to deceive the Republican voters, that he had conspired with the communist element in the Democratic Party to receive their support, and that he was disloyal to his country. The "tabloid" was then widely distributed to prospective Republican voters. After several insufficient attempts to amend his complaint to adequately state a cause of action for libel, the trial court sustained the opponent's demurrer. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that both the conspiracy count and the libel count insufficiently alleged actual malice because there was no indication that the candidate claimed that the opponent had any purpose in mind except to defeat him at the polls.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the opponent's demurrer to the candidate's libel and conspiracy claims.

 

1331 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Dudley


Civ. No. 22407


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


239 Cal. App. 2d 401; 48 Cal. Rptr. 790; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1774



January 18, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 16, 1966. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Alameda County vacating that part of an order committing respondent's daughter to placement in the Sonoma State Home and providing that respondent pay the sum of $ 20 per month to the county for her daughter's care. John J. Purchio, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) vacating that part of an order committing respondent's daughter to placement in a state home and providing that respondent pay the county for her daughter's care.


OVERVIEW: Respondent alleged that her daughter, aged 18, was in need of closer supervision than she could give her; that she had evaded supervision, left her home and was criminally assaulted, and had been classified as an imbecile by a psychologist. Respondent sought an order committing her daughter to a state home and providing for the payment of the expenses of the proceeding and of the delivery and care of her daughter in the institution. The court stated that it was not unconstitutional to require contribution from a person otherwise responsible for the care of a mentally deficient person, within that person's ability to pay. The court concluded that it would be a gift of public money to furnish institutional care, support, and treatment to a person of means without securing recompense from his estate. Therefore, neither a wealthy parent, nor the parent of an indigent mentally retarded adult child, who had been found to be charged with, and able to pay a portion of the support of such child should receive such benefaction from the county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, which vacating an order committing respondent's daughter to placement in a state home and providing that respondent pay the county for her daughter's care.
