People v. Harris


Crim. No. 9982


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


239 Cal. App. 2d 393; 48 Cal. Rptr. 677; 1966 Cal. App. LEXIS 1773



January 17, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Mark Brandler, Judge.

Prosecution for endangering the life or health of children.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County(California), which convicted her of endangering the life or health of children in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 273a. Defendant was charged with a codefendant and both pled not guilty and waived trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: After a complaint from a neighbor, a police officer visited defendant's house. He found several small children in the house, three of whom were defendant's. The officer found the house to be filthy with old food and excrement all over. At least one of the children was raw on his legs and buttocks where a sheet that had dried to him had been ripped off. Defendant was found guilty. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that § 273a was constitutional in that it gave sufficient notice of the type of activity which was prohibited by it and was not void for vagueness. The court found that expert testimony to show what situation would be hazardous to the children. The court found that the information sufficiently informed defendant of the crime she was charged with and was not insufficient for failing to allege that she had the care or custody of the children. The court additionally found that defendant did not demur to the information as required by Cal. Penal Code § 1004 or make a motion in arrest of the judgment as required by Cal. Penal Code § 1012.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of endangering the life or health of children.

 

1333 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gilmore


Crim. No. 10875


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


239 Cal. App. 2d 125; 48 Cal. Rptr. 449; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1102



December 30, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 23, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Newell Barrett, Judge.

Prosecution for illegal sale of narcotics.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant of a sale of heroin, a violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11501, with four prior felony convictions, two of which were for narcotic violations. Defendant's motions for a new trial and probation were denied.


OVERVIEW: Police implemented a "buy" program in which an informant introduced officers to sundry narcotic sellers and arranged for sales to have been made by the persons introduced. The program lasted for approximately four months. On appeal from his conviction, defendant contended that he was denied due process of law in that there was an undue delay between the date of the offense charged and the date of his arrest. The court rejected the contention that defendant was denied any constitutional rights by reason of the fact that his case was not presented to the Grand Jury until a little over two months after it occurred. The court concluded that there was no showing that the delay was not for a valid reason nor that it prejudiced defendant. Further, the court held that the pre-arrest delay case was supported by a commendably legitimate reason. The court further rejected defendant's contention that he was unconstitutionally deprived of his right to interview and to subpoena a police informer because the informer disappeared. The court reasoned that there was no showing that prosecution was delayed in order that the informer might disappear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

People v. Glaser


Crim. No. 4883


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


238 Cal. App. 2d 819; 48 Cal. Rptr. 427; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1203



December 20, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 16, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Leonard J. Dieden, Judge.

Prosecution for the illegal possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which convicted him of illegal possession of marijuana in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was taken into custody after violating Cal. Penal Code § 836(1), and then, because he was acting strangely, he was then taken to a hospital to determine if he needed treatment. The doctor diagnosed his condition as an influence of some type of drug. The officer searched defendant and found a bottle of pills and a marijuana cigarette butt. Defendant was arrested and was later convicted of illegal possession of marijuana, after representing himself in court. He appealed, arguing, inter alia, that the statute was unconstitutional, the trial court erred in not advising him of his constitutional rights before permitting him to testify, and the marijuana was taken under an illegal search and seizure. The court affirmed, holding that even if the statute was unconstitutional for failing to recognize exceptions of legal possession, defendant did not show himself to be one of the class which he claimed was aggrieved. The court also held that the failure to advise defendant of his right to refrain from testifying could not be ground for attack because he volunteered to testify, and the evidence taken in the search at the hospital was justified and lawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for illegal possession of marijuana.

 

1335 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Lees v. Bay Area Air Pollution Control Dist.


Civ. No. 22388


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


238 Cal. App. 2d 850; 48 Cal. Rptr. 295; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1205



December 20, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 19, 1966, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 16, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to have a regulation limiting the use of incinerators declared unconstitutional, or to compel the granting of a variance from the regulation.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant apartment owners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied their petition for a writ of mandate to declare Regulation 2 of respondent Bay Area Air Pollution Control District (district) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The apartment owners owned a building that housed more than two families. The district adopted a regulation imposing limitations upon the emission of dense smoke from a number of sources, including incinerators. The regulation was applicable to apartment house incinerators, but exempt those used in one and two-family dwellings. The apartment owners unsuccessfully brought an action to have the superior court declare the regulation unconstitutional because it confiscated their property without just compensation and created an arbitrary classification. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The court stated that in creating the regulation, the district was engaged in an exercise of the state's police power. As the evident purpose of the regulation was to protect the purity of the air, the court stated that the regulation was not only reasonable, but also essential and represented a lawful and proper exercise of the police power. The court found that the regulation applied equally to all multi-family housing units and all within that class were treated alike. Therefore, the regulation was not an arbitrary or unreasonable classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the apartment owners' writ of mandate.

 

1336 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Patterson v. Missler


Civ. No. 7467


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


238 Cal. App. 2d 759; 48 Cal. Rptr. 215; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1196



December 16, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was denied January 3, 1966, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 9, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Robert W. Conyers, Judge.

Action by creditors to set aside an allegedly fraudulent conveyance of real property.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiffs reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant bona fide purchaser appealed an order from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which on plaintiff creditors' motion set aside a conveyance of real property to defendant by an insolvent as fraudulent under the Uniform Fraudulent Conveyance Act (Act), Cal. Civ. Code § 3439.01-3439.12. Defendant claimed that the lower court did not protect defendant's rights as required by the Act.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff creditors brought an action against an insolvent and defendant bona fide purchaser to set aside a conveyance of real property by the insolvent to defendant as fraudulent under the Uniform Fraudulent Conveyance Act (Act), Cal. Civ. Code § 3439.01-3439.12. The lower court ruled in favor of plaintiff and defendant appealed on the basis that the judgment ordering the sale of the property at issue failed to protect defendant's rights under the Act. The court agreed and reversed and remanded the judgment. The court held that the procedure outlined by the lower court's order to satisfy plaintiff's judgment against the insolvent was incomplete because the lower court erred in determining the amount of defendant's lien on the property as a bona fide purchaser pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 3439.09, as the determination failed to provide for interest on defendant's original investment from the date of investment to the date of judgment. The court also found that the judgment failed to provide for the payment to defendant of the balance, if any, of the sale proceeds after payment to plaintiff of the amount of their money judgment against the insolvent.


OUTCOME: A judgment ordering the sale of property fraudulently conveyed to defendant bona fide purchaser to satisfy a money judgment of plaintiff creditors against insolvent was reversed and remanded on the grounds that the lower court failed to properly calculate defendant's lien and rights to the sale proceeds of the property as conferred under relevant state statute.

 

1337 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Palacio


Crim. No. 11399


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


238 Cal. App. 2d 545; 48 Cal. Rptr. 50; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1169



December 3, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to prevent confinement in county jail pursuant to order of commitment issued by summary court-martial.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an enlisted member of the California Air National Guard, sought a writ of habeas corpus to prevent his confinement in county jail pursuant to an order of commitment issued by a summary court-martial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the denial of assistance of counsel before the summary court-martial violated his constitutional rights. The court found that it was unnecessary to determine whether the right-to-counsel guarantees of either the United States or California Constitution were applicable to trials in military courts. Even if it were assumed that constitutional guarantees of the right to counsel applied in military trials, such guarantees were protected or satisfied when an accused before a summary court-martial was entitled to object to such summary proceeding and to be tried instead by a special or general court-martial in which the right to counsel was secured by military law. The provisions of Unif. Code Mil. Justice art. 20, 10 U.S.C.S. § 820, with reference to the right to object to trial by summary court-martial was applicable to members of the California Air National Guard. The court found that the ordered commitment resulted from proceedings in which petitioner was denied a basic right and procedure because he was denied the right to object to trial by summary court-martial and to be tried by special court-martial wherein he would have the assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ.

 

1338 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Arthur Murray, Inc.


Civ. No. 29224


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


238 Cal. App. 2d 333; 47 Cal. Rptr. 700; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1146



November 23, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 13, 1965, and the Petition of Appellant Arthur Murray, Inc., for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 19, 1966. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from an order of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County granting a preliminary injunction against the sale of dance lesson contracts in violation of the Health or Dance Studio Act ( Civ. Code, § 1812.80 et seq.) C. Douglas Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; appeals of certain persons dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State filed a complaint against defendant corporation that sought to enjoin the corporation and its agents from violating the Health or Dance Studio Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 1812.80 et seq. (act). The Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California) granted the preliminary injunction against the sale of lifetime dance lesson contracts, which violated the act. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that the record did not show that it had ever violated the provisions of the act, that is, that it did not contract directly with the dance students, but that its agents contracted directly with the students. The corporation further argued that the act was unconstitutional. The court held that the record supported the inference that the corporation continued to aid, and encouraged, the agents to violate the act. Thus, the corporation participated in the admitted statutory violations of the agents. The act was found to be constitutional because there was an adequate basis for invoking special regulations of a class of business so habitually fraught with fraud and with sharp practices. The purpose of the act was to limit the number of lessons which a studio may contract to give in any one contract. The injunction was a more effective remedy than retroactive relief in damages, and prevention was the essence of the public benefit which the act sought to protect.


OUTCOME: The order granting preliminary injunction against the corporation was affirmed.

California State Employees Asso. v. Trustees of California State Colleges


Civ. No. 22169


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


237 Cal. App. 2d 530; 47 Cal. Rptr. 73; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1285



October 20, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 15, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Action for an injunction and for a writ of mandate to compel the Trustees of the California State Colleges and the State Personnel Board to establish classifications, hold competitive examinations and to effect all civil service requirements for certain nonacademic employees of the state colleges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to the complaint was sustained without leave to amend affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state employees association (association) sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which dismissed, by sustaining a demurrer to the complaint without leave to amend, a mandamus action to compel respondents, state college trustees and state personnel board (state), to treat certain nonacademic employees of the state colleges as civil service employees.


OVERVIEW: The association filed a mandamus action seeking an injunction to compel the state to apply all civil service procedures and requirements to nonacademic employees of the state colleges. It contended that Pol. Code § 362a et seq. (1921), which placed state teachers colleges and their employees under the state department of education's control, effectively made it impossible for the employees to be covered by the exception from civil service of "persons employed by any state normal school or teachers college" under Cal. Const. art. XXIV, § 4(a)(8). It argued that this was the case because, under § 362a, the nonacademic employees were defined as employees of the Director of Education, and not of the state colleges. The trial court dismissed the action with prejudice upon the state's demurrer. On appeal, the court affirmed and noted that a person was generally considered employed by the institution for which he worked, and reasoned that the legislature would not have enacted the constitutional civil service exception in 1934 had it intended the particular language therein to immediately be a nullity. The court concluded that the employees thus were excepted from civil service.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the state's demurrer to the association's complaint and dismissing the action.

Ferris v. Industrial Accident Comm'n


Civ. No. 7753


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


237 Cal. App. 2d 427; 46 Cal. Rptr. 913; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1268; 30 Cal. Comp. Cases 311



October 7, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Respondent State Compensation Insurance Fund for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 1, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING to review a decision of the Industrial Accident Commission and an order denying a petition for reconsideration of an award of compensation for personal injuries.



DISPOSITION: Award annulled and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner policeman sought review of an order of respondent Industrial Accident Commission (California) that awarded him apportioned compensation for a heart injury that he sustained in the course of his employment for respondent city.


OVERVIEW: The employee suffered angina on his day off from work. It was discovered that the employee's angina was caused by his arteriosclerotic condition. The Commission found that the policeman sustained an injury to his heart arising out of his employment and, after apportionment, set the rate of permanent disability caused by the injury. The employee argued on appeal that all of his permanent disability should have been charged against the city. The court annulled the Commission's order. The court held that the Commission was not permitted to apportion the policeman's heart condition to his nonindustrial condition under Cal. Lab. Code § 3212.5. Cal. Lab. Code § 4663, allowing apportionment, was inapplicable to situations covered by Cal. Lab. Code § 3212.5. Section 3212.5 was constitutional under Cal. Const. art. XX, § 21.


OUTCOME: The order that awarded the policeman apportioned compensation for a heart injury was annulled and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1341 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Plum v. Healdsburg


Civ. No. 22316


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


237 Cal. App. 2d 308; 46 Cal. Rptr. 827; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1258



September 30, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 22, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sonoma County. Lilburn Gibson, Judge. *


* Retired judge of the superior court sitting under assignment by the chairman of the Judicial Council.

Proceedings in mandamus to compel a city building inspector to issue a building permit.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment granting writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city, building inspector, and city council, challenged the conclusions of law and writ of mandate of the Superior Court of Sonoma County (California), which ordered that a writ of mandate be issued to compel the inspector to issue a building permit to respondent property owners in their proceeding in mandamus to compel the building inspector to issue a building permit to allow construction of a trailer camp on their property.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, in the form of a conclusion of law, determined that the property owners were entitled to the issuance of a writ of mandate directing the building inspector to issue a building permit for their construction of a trailer camp. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the determination of the planning commission to permit a trailer camp was not in conformance with the provisions of the city zoning ordinance and, therefore, was null and void, which gave the building inspector justification in refusing to issue the building permit for that reason. The court found that the building inspector, as a ministerial officer, could not refuse to issue a building permit unless the planning commission's determination and approval were not in conformance with the city ordinance. The court ruled that the action of the planning commission did not require the approval of the city council because the ordinance did not contain any provisions for review of the planning commission's determination that a trailer camp was a similar use as those listed in the particular zoning permit and, therefore, its decision could not be overturned by the city council.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in favor of appellants and directed the trial court to amend its conclusions of law to provide that the property owners were not entitled to a peremptory writ of mandate and to enter a judgment denying the property owners a peremptory writ of mandate and discharging the alternative writ in the property owners' proceeding in mandamus seeking a building permit.

Kirby v. Municipal Court for Newhall Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 28898


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


237 Cal. App. 2d 335; 46 Cal. Rptr. 844; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1260



September 30, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 24, 1965. Peters, J., Tobriner, J., and Peek, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. A. Curtis Smith, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain a municipal court from proceeding further in a criminal action.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner criminal appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), denying his application for a writ of prohibition barring his prosecution for violating a municipal ordinance criminalizing advertisements for the sale of obscene materials.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner criminal appealed a judgment denying his application for a writ of prohibition barring his prosecution for violation of an obscene materials ordinance. The court affirmed the denial of the application. Petitioner was charged in an inferior court with a misdemeanor, it being alleged that he unlawfully produced an advertisement promoting the sale of obscene materials. Petitioner then sought prohibition, maintaining that the ordinance outlawing such advertisements was unconstitutional since it did not require a mental state. In petitioner's view, the ordinance's failure to mandate proof that the person charged knew the material in question was obscene was a fatal defect. In rejecting this argument, the court held that it was enough that the person charged have deliberately produced the advertisement; the person's lack of knowledge that the material was obscene was of no moment. Since the court below was correct on the law, the application for a writ of prohibition was correctly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1343 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fisherman


Crim. No. 10348


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


237 Cal. App. 2d 356; 47 Cal. Rptr. 33; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1262



September 30, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 22, 1965, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 22, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. J. Howard Ziemann, Judge.

Prosecution for the illegal sale of heroin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied his motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction a proceeding at which defendant was sentenced to a state prison for the remaining term prescribed for his conviction for violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11501 after his guilty plea to heroin sales. The court had previously revoked defendant's probation at a proceeding in his absence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the trial court's action, sentencing him to a state prison for the term prescribed for his violation of § 11501. The court revoked defendant's probation and sentenced him in his absence to serve the remainder of his sentence, based on defendant's violation of his parole for an unrelated prior robbery conviction. The court on appeal affirmed the trial court's judgment based on its determination that (1) the trial court did not lose jurisdiction over defendant because of an inadvertent clerical error in its commitment order, which originally made reference to the wrong statute, and defendant suffered no prejudice from the court's action; (2) the revocation of defendant's probation and the imposition of his sentence, accomplished in defendant's absence and without a waiver of his right to be present and represented by counsel, was void but did not destroy the validity of the original probation order, because defendant's status remained the same with the imposition of his suspended sentence; and (3) because defendant's probation was reinstated on the same terms imposed when it was originally granted, his rights were not violated by his hearing absence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1344 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Shell Oil Co. v. State Bd. of Equalization


Civ. 10953


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


46 Cal. Rptr. 653; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1591



September 28, 1965, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Modified October 25, 1965.
Rehearing denied by Shell Oil Co. v. State Bd. of Equalization, 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1592 (Cal. App. 3d Dist., Oct. 25, 1965)
Superseded by Shell Oil Co. v. State Board of Equalization, 64 Cal. 2d 713, 414 P.2d 820, 1966 Cal. LEXIS 304, 51 Cal. Rptr. 524 (1966)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company sought review of a decision from a trial court (California), which granted judgment for respondents, the State of California and the State of Board of Equalization, on the oil company's action seeking a refund of the taxes paid under protest which were imposed on sales of "bunker" fuel oil for consumption on ships engaged in foreign and interstate commerce.


OVERVIEW: The oil company filed suit against the State and the State of Board of Equalization, seeking a refund of taxes paid under protest. The oil company challenged the State's power to impose retail sales tax on the company's sales of fuel oil for consumption on ships engaged in foreign and interstate commerce. The company claimed that the tax violated the import-export clause of the constitution, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 2, and claimed immunity from state taxation under the interstate and foreign commerce clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The court affirmed the portion of the judgment denying a refund of taxes on fuel oil supplied to vessels in interstate commerce and concluded that the vessel's fuel was not itself an "export" and the tax did not unduly burden interstate commerce. The court reversed the judgment denying a refund of sales taxes on fuel oil supplied to vessels engaged exclusively in the export trade and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court ruled that the tax was a levy on the ocean transportation of export cargo, burdening a necessity of the voyage, and was precisely the kind of economic barrier the import-export clause was designed to prevent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying a refund of sales taxes on fuel oil supplied by the oil company to vessels engaged in interstate commerce. The court reversed the portion of the judgment denying a refund of sales taxes on fuel oil supplied to vessels engaged exclusively in the export trade, and the cause was remanded to the lower court for further proceedings.

 

1345 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Camara v. Municipal Court of San Francisco


Civ. No. 22128


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


237 Cal. App. 2d 128; 46 Cal. Rptr. 585; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1237



September 22, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 16, 1965. Peters, J., and Peek, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco denying a writ of prohibition. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain the Municipal Court of the City and County of San Francisco from taking further proceedings in a criminal case arising out of a violation of the city's housing code.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Order denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), denying a writ of prohibition to restrain the Municipal Court of the City and County of San Francisco from taking further proceedings in a criminal case arising from a violation of the city's housing code.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Public Health was required to make an annual inspection of all San Francisco apartment houses for the purpose of licensing such apartment houses and issuing permits of occupancy. Defendant was arrested and charged with violation of the San Francisco, Cal., Housing Code § 507. Defendant admitted he committed the offense proscribed by § 507, but argued that § 503 was unconstitutional. Defendant asserted that § 503 authorized an unreasonable search and seizure, in violation of Cal. Const. art. I, § 19, and the Fourth Amendment to the federal Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. IV, as applied to the states through the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed. The court found that § 503 was part of a regulatory scheme, which was essentially civil rather than criminal in nature, inasmuch as that section created a right of inspection which was limited in scope and may not be exercised under unreasonable conditions. The ordinance was thus no broader in scope than ordinances that were upheld, and defendant's constitutional objections failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the writ of prohibition.

 

1346 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mobin


Crim. No. 5175


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


237 Cal. App. 2d 115; 46 Cal. Rptr. 605; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1235



September 20, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 16, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment (order granting probation) of the Municipal Court for the Richmond Judicial District of Contra Costa County. * John I. Pierce, Judge.


* Reporter's Note: The appeal was transferred to the District Court of Appeal after certification by the Appellate Department of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County. (See California Rules of Court, rules 62, 63.)

Prosecution for engaging in door-to-door solicitation without obtaining a municipal permit to do so.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Municipal Court for the Richmond Judicial District of Contra Costa County (California) that convicted them of engaging in door to door solicitation without first obtaining a written permit from the chief of police in violation of City of Richmond, Cal., Mun. Code § 7.40.030.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of violating § 7.40.030 after they engaged in door to door sales of cutlery without first obtaining a written permit from the chief of police. Defendants appealed, and the court affirmed. The enactment of § 7.40.030 was a proper exercise of the city's police power. A municipality could in the exercise of its police power enact reasonable regulations relating to the activities of those persons who engaged in door to door solicitation. Such regulations could include the requirement that the solicitor obtain a permit. It was further proper for the city to impose a nominal fee for the issuance of a license to solicitors because the license fee had a reasonable relation to the expense of investigation, issuing the license, and regulating the activities within the purview of the license. The imposition of a fee here was not an undue burden on interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1347 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hampton


Crim. No. 11108


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


236 Cal. App. 2d 795; 46 Cal. Rptr. 338; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 876



August 25, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 20, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court of the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County. Donald M. Redwine, Judge.

Prosecution for paying wages with an instrument not backed by sufficient funds.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought to overturn their convictions for violating Cal. Lab. Code § 212(a). The Appellate Department of the Los Angeles County Superior Court (California), had affirmed a conviction by the municipal court.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were officers of a corporation and signed paychecks that were dishonored. Their only defense was that their corporation had an agreement with private investors who were supposed to fund the corporation's accounts and that they had no actual knowledge of the deficiency in the bank accounts upon which the checks were written. The lower court affirmed the convictions of defendants, and the court affirmed the lower court. The court held that Cal. Lab. Code § 212(a) established a presumption that the drawee of a check was guilty of violation if the check was dishonored. The presumption of a violation could be rebutted by drawees if they showed what precautions they took to make sure that sufficient funds were in the bank account. However, the presumption was not rebutted by defendants when they testified that they simply had no actual knowledge of the insufficiency in the bank account.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of defendants for a violation of the California Labor Code.

 

1348 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Butts


Crim. No. 3558


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


236 Cal. App. 2d 817; 46 Cal. Rptr. 362; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 879



August 25, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Appellant Otwell for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 10, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Butte County. Jean Morony, Judge.

Prosecution of two defendants for murder, conspiracy to commit assault and assault with intent to commit murder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions. Judgment convicting one defendant of second degree murder, conspiracy to commit assault and assault with intent to commit murder affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions; judgment convicting other defendant of involuntary manslaughter, conspiracy and simple assault reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Butte County (California) that convicted one defendant for second-degree murder, conspiracy to commit assault, and assault with intent to commit murder and the other defendant for involuntary manslaughter, conspiracy, and simple assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were jointly indicted upon conspiracy to commit assault, murder of first victim, assault upon second victim with intent to commit murder, and assault with intent to commit murder upon third victim. A jury found defendant one guilty on all four counts, fixing the homicide as second-degree murder. The jury returned verdicts finding defendant two guilty of conspiracy to commit assault, involuntary manslaughter as an included lesser offense, and simple assault upon victims two and three as included lesser offenses. New trial motions were denied and judgments pronounced. Both defendants appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that, although, as a means of testing the character witness' knowledge of reputation, the district attorney could ask the witness whether he had heard of specific acts of misconduct, he could not ask the witness whether he knew of specific acts of misconduct. The court held that conviction of second degree murder required no proof of premeditation or even of actual intent to take life. The court noted that the reversal of the conspiracy conviction thus necessitated reversal of the assault convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The judgment that convicted defendant one of second-degree murder was affirmed, but convictions for conspiracy to commit assault and assault with intent to commit murder were reversed. The judgment that convicted defendant two of involuntary manslaughter, conspiracy and simple assault was reversed. The court ordered the dismissal of the conspiracy charges for both defendants.

 

1349 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Taliaferro v. Hoogs


Civ. No. 22218


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


236 Cal. App. 2d 521; 46 Cal. Rptr. 147; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 847



August 16, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County. Norman A. Gregg, Judge.

Cross-complaint for damages for alleged conspiracy to withhold sums allegedly due.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment dismissing cross-complaint as vexatious litigation affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties filed cross-complaints for damages for alleged conspiracy to withhold sums allegedly due. The Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California) ordered appellant to furnish security to the court pursuant to the vexatious litigant statute, Cal. Code Civ. Proc. §§ 391- 391.6. The superior court dismissed appellant's complaint after he failed to furnish the security. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the judgment of dismissal must be reversed because (1) the statute was unconstitutional, and (2) even if constitutional, there was no evidence that he was a vexatious litigant as defined by the statute. The court rejected these contentions, finding that (1) the statutory language referencing no "reasonable probability" that the alleged vexatious litigant would prevail was not unconstitutionally vague; (2) the constitutional guarantee of a jury trial, Cal. Const. art. I, § 7 did not apply in this special proceeding because it was not expressly made available by statute; (3) appellant failed to demand a jury trial and his failure to do so constituted a waiver under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 631; (4) respondent's detailed affidavit related more than enough of the required litigations to bring appellant within the definition of a vexatious litigant and appellant failed to present any counter-affidavits; (5) the trial court did not err in failing to make findings because findings were not required in this special proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed appellant's cross-complaint as vexatious litigation.

 

1350 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Rich v. State Board of Optometry


Civ. Nos. 21797, 21961


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


235 Cal. App. 2d 591; 45 Cal. Rptr. 512; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 960



July 7, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 28, 1965, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 2, 1965. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Proceedings in mandamus to compel the State Board of Optometry to issue branch office licenses.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments granting writs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff optometrists petitioned in mandamus to compel defendants, California State Board of Optometry and its members (board), to issue branch office licenses to allow them to transfer branch offices that already were in existence to different locations. The Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) overruled the board's demurrer and peremptory writs of mandate were granted to the optometrists. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The optometrists were duly licensed and, prior to the 1959 amendments to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 3077 (1955) (amended 1959), operated several branches throughout the San Francisco area. Prior to 1959, although the optometrists had to obtain licenses for each branch office, there was no limitation on the number of such branches. After the 1959 amendments, § 3077(f) limited to one the number of branch office licenses that would be issued to an optometrist or two or more optometrists jointly. However, § 3077(i) provided a grandfather clause to then-existing branches, with that privilege terminating upon the sale of the branch office. The board argued that the transfer of branch offices would constitute a sale. The court disagreed, holding that: (1) Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1085 was applicable as the judicial relief sought was the issuance of a judicial writ, not an appeal from the board's findings and, thus, the optometrists' appeal was timely; and (2) a transfer of the branches would not constitute a sale as § 3077(i) gave protection not to the specifically located branches, but to the number of branch offices operated by an optometrist prior to the 1959 amendment's effective date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of peremptory writs of mandate to the optometrists that compelled the board to issue licenses to the optometrists for the transfer of their branch offices to different locations.

Harris v. Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board


Civ. No. 22304


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


235 Cal. App. 2d 479; 45 Cal. Rptr. 450; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 947



June 29, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 29, 1965, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 25, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Joseph Karesh, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board to set aside and vacate an order reversing a decision of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control denying issuance of a beer and wine license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Director of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied his petition for writ of mandate to set aside and vacate an order of respondent Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board that reversed the decision of the Department denying issuance of a beer and wine license to respondent restaurant owners.


OVERVIEW: The Department denied the restaurant owners' application for a conditional on-sale beer and wine license. The Board reversed the Department's decision. The Department brought a proceeding in mandamus to compel the Board to reverse its decision. The superior court denied the petition for writ of mandate, and the Department appealed. The court held that: (1) Cal. Admin. Code tit. 4, § 61.1, upon which the Department based its denial of the license, was void because it was in conflict with Cal. Penal Code § 172e; and (2) the Department's denial of the license was based solely on its application of § 61.1, and it made no independent determination that the granting of the license would be contrary to public welfare and morals. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment denying the writ of mandate.

 

1352 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Kaneda v. Kaneda


Civ. No. 21964


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


235 Cal. App. 2d 404; 45 Cal. Rptr. 437; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 940



June 28, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. John D. Foley, Judge.

Action for partition of certain real property and cross-action to establish that the property was held under a resulting trust for the benefit of the heirs of the original owner.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment declaring property to be held under a resulting trust affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which declared that certain property was held under a resulting trust in the claimant's action against defendant brother for partition of the real property.


OVERVIEW: The claimant brought an action against his brother for partition of the parcel of real property, alleging that he and his brother owned the property as tenants in common by virtue of a deed from an attorney. Following the trial court's declaration of a resulting trust, the claimant appealed. The court affirmed. Pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 853, the payment of the purchase price by the claimant's deceased father and the taking of title in the name of the attorney gave rise to a presumption that the attorney held the title in trust for the decedent. The evidence clearly supported the trial court's finding that the claimant and his brother received title to the property without consideration, with knowledge of the existence of the trust in favor of the decedent and his heirs, and subject to that trust. The conditions no longer prevailed, which evoked the declaration that the presumption of § 853 did not apply where property was purchased by an alien ineligible to hold it. The court concluded that knowledge of grave injustices done under the guise of the Alien Land Act led to the conclusion that the trial court did not err in finding a resulting trust in favor of the decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment declaring the property to be held under a resulting trust in the claimant's action against his brother for partition of the real property.

 

1353 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Stephan v. Proctor


Civ. No. 28489


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


235 Cal. App. 2d 228; 45 Cal. Rptr. 124; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 923



June 22, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 18, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. F. Ray Bennett, Judge.

Action for personal injuries sustained while riding in an automobile.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of nonsuit on opening statement to the jury affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In her action for personal injuries sustained while riding in defendant driver's automobile, plaintiff guest appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted a motion for nonsuit following the guest's opening statement to the jury, although supplemented by additional facts.


OVERVIEW: The driver was going through a divorce and the guest, her roommate, offered to take her to dinner. They decided to take the driver's car because the guest's car was a convertible with the top down and the driver did not want to muss her hair. They stopped at a bar, and an accident happened on their way home. The guest alleged that she was a passenger, rather than a guest under Cal. Veh. Code § 17158. The court affirmed the grant of the motion for nonsuit and held that the conclusion was inescapable that no tangible benefit served as the principal inducement for the driver furnishing the guest a ride. There was no contention that there was either wilful misconduct or intoxication for an exception to § 17158. The purpose of the evening was purely social in nature and the benefit conferred was not for the ride but for the pleasure of the driver's company during the evening's festivities and in the guest's hope that she could in some way relieve the driver of her worries, which did not constitute compensation within the meaning of § 17158. As such, she was a guest, there was no viable compensation to preclude the application of § 17158, and § 17158 barred her action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Wenzler v. Municipal Court for Pasadena Judicial Dist.

1355 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Niagara Fire Ins. Co. v. Cole


Civ. No. 437


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


235 Cal. App. 2d 40; 44 Cal. Rptr. 889; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 900



June 10, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Joseph L. Joy, Judge.

Action by an insurer against its assured for declaratory relief and for an injunction to restrain the assured from proceeding under the uninsured motorist statute with an arbitration hearing on a claim for injuries.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which, in respondent insurer's action for declaratory relief and for an injunction to restrain the insured from proceeding under the uninsured motorist statute with an arbitration hearing on her claim for damages for injuries allegedly sustained, held in favor of the insurer and found that the claim was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: On April 4, 1960, while driving a vehicle covered by the insurer's policy, the insured was injured; the driver of the other vehicle involved was unknown. Within 30 days, the insured filed a statement with the insurer concerning the accident, as required by the policy relating to uninsured motorist coverage. On July 17, 1963, the insured demanded damages for bodily injuries and demanded arbitration. Following the demand, the instant action was commenced. The court affirmed. Prior to Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.2(h) (effective September 15, 1961), the uninsured motorist statute embodied no period of limitations governing causes of action accruing thereunder so that general statutes limiting the filing of actions were applicable. However, § 11580.2(h) imposed a one-year period of limitations. The court held that § 11580.2(h) could not be applied retrospectively to cut off the insured's claim; however, even by a prospective application beginning on September 15, 1961, the insured was beyond the one-year period of limitations. The court held that one-year was a reasonable time for the insured to have brought the action, and her failure to do so barred her claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

In re Cavanaugh


Civ. No. 22056


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


234 Cal. App. 2d 316; 44 Cal. Rptr. 422; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1018



May 12, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 8, 1965, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 7, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sonoma County extending term of control over a youth committed to the Youth Authority. Hilliard Comstock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant minor challenged the Superior Court of Sonoma County's (California) decision extending the control of plaintiff youth authority over the minor for a period of two years beyond his 21st birthday pursuant to the youth authority's action brought under Cal. Welf. & Inst. §§ 1800 through 1803.


OVERVIEW: The minor was committed to the youth authority when he was 14 years of age. A physician that examined the minor concluded that he was a dangerous person and able to kill someone. Later examinations by various psychiatrists confirmed this evaluation. During his detention, the minor was paroled three times, and each time his parole was revoked because of failure to adjust in society. The control of the youth authority over the minor would ordinarily have ceased upon the minor's 21st birthday, but as that date approached it appeared that the minor was not prepared to make any successful adjustment outside of some correctional facility. The youth authority then sought to continue the minor's detention. On appeal, the minor contended that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to issue the order extending the minor's detention because the youth authority did not comply with procedural requirements concerning the filing of the petition. The court held that Cal. Welf. & Inst. § 1800, which required that a petition be filed at least 90 days before the date of discharge did not purport to restrict the trial court's power to act. Therefore, the court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to extend the minor's detention in the youth authority's action seeking to extend the minor's detention at the correctional facility.

 

1357 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


White v. Valenta


Civ. No. 27640


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


234 Cal. App. 2d 243; 44 Cal. Rptr. 241; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1010; 13 A.L.R.3d 1271



May 6, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 30, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Charles C. Stratton, Judge.

Action for slander uttered by an intruder on a live television broadcast.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighboring businessman challenged, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code §§ 46, 48a, a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which ruled that appellant had uttered slander against respondent automobile business owner as an intruder on a live television broadcast. A jury assessed compensatory and punitive damages against appellant. The matter came before the court on a settled statement.


OVERVIEW: The court asserted that this case was not a proper one for drawing sweeping parallels between persons whom Cal. Civ. Code § 48a protected in the newspaper business and those covered in television. The court found no request for a ruling at the trial that gave appellant neighboring businessman the benefit of § 48a if he was unaware that he was publishing his remarks through television. The court found that the jury believed respondent automobile business owner's witnesses. The court asserted that the amount of punitive damages awarded showed that the jury did not believe appellant, even though it was instructed to consider provocation, mistake, or ignorance of facts or other circumstances that might mitigate appellant's culpability. The court held that § 48a did not protect an intruder and concluded that if by innuendo and inducement his words were susceptible of a defamatory meaning pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 46(3), no special damages had to be pleaded or proved. The court asserted that the jury found that appellant's remarks imputed to respondent a general disqualification in aspects that his occupation peculiarly required, such as fair dealing. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment favoring respondent automobile business owner. Appellant neighboring businessman was an intruder and was not covered by the statute, and no special damages had to be pleaded or proved. Appellant's remarks generally disqualified respondent in the area of fair dealing and were slanderous.

 

1358 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


California Democratic Council v. Arnebergh


Civ. No. 28396


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


233 Cal. App. 2d 425; 43 Cal. Rptr. 531; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1376; 5 Rad. Reg. 2d (P & F) 2073



April 5, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 23, 1965, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 2, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Shirley M. Hufstedler, Judge.

Action seeking an injunction and a declaration that certain legislation concerning the endorsement of candidates for public office in primary elections is unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, political group and related individuals (group), sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted judgment in favor of defendant government officials in the group's action seeking an injunction and a declaration that certain sections of the Truth in Endorsements Law (Law), Cal. Elec. Code § 8600 et seq. were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Law provided that every advertisement that made reference to any candidate for nomination for partisan office in a direct primary and contained a statement to the effect that the candidate had been endorsed by an organization using as a part of its name the name of a political party, was to bear a notice that the organization was an unofficial political group. The group was a group of volunteer, unpaid party members not acting in any official party capacity and did not want to comply with the Law's notice requirements. The court determined that the Law was constitutional. Cal. Const. art. II, § 2 1/2 expressly empowered the legislature to establish tests governing the rights of political parties to participate in primary elections. The Law served to attain the legitimate objective of requiring that all party nominations be made directly by members of the party at a primary election. Furthermore, Cal. Elec. Code § 8601(4) provided that the voting public was entitled to protection by law from deception in political campaigns. The Law did not curtail the right to endorse any candidate, it merely required that the use of a name of a political party not mislead the voters.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision.

 

1359 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. San Carlos


Civ. No. 21759


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


233 Cal. App. 2d 290; 43 Cal. Rptr. 486; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1362



March 30, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County and from an order denying a motion for reconsideration. Wayne R. Millington, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a city to rescind an ordinance and to cancel a contract with the county for assessment and collection of city taxes, entered into under authority of such ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to the complaint was sustained without leave to amend affirmed; motion to dismiss appeal denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision for respondents, city and city officials, by the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) in a petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the city to rescind a municipal ordinance and cancel a contract entered under the authority of the ordinance. The taxpayer appealed the denial of his motion for reconsideration of the denial of his petition.


OVERVIEW: By ordinance, the city and the county entered into a contract for the county to collect the city's taxes. The taxpayer sought to have the trial court rescind the contract and void the ordinance on constitutional grounds. The trial court denied the taxpayer's request and his motion to reconsider the denial. The court affirmed the decision against the taxpayer. Though at the time of the action, Cal. Const. art. XI, § 6 may have required a vote by the electorate to enter into the contract, Proposition 11 eliminated that requirement and retroactively validated such contracts. The ordinance did not violate Cal. Gov't Code § 45007 by the elimination of city officials' duties to collect taxes because Cal. Gov't Code § 51506 allowed for the transfer of those duties. The electorate did not have the power to determine the structure of the city government because the city was a general law city and, thus, was a creature of the state, which controlled its structure. The taxpayer had his right to vote on whether the city could have transferred its tax collection powers to the county in the statewide election of Proposition 11. The denial of the motion for reconsideration was not appealable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for the city and the city officials and against the taxpayer in the petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the city to rescind a municipal ordinance and cancel a contract entered under the authority of the ordinance and in the denial of the taxpayer's motion for reconsideration of the denial of his petition.

County of L.A. v. Superior Court

1361 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Aguirre v. Southern Pacific Co.


Civ. No. 10901


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


232 Cal. App. 2d 636; 43 Cal. Rptr. 73; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1510; 30 Cal. Comp. Cases 453



March 4, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Elvin F. Sheehy, Judge.

Action by an employee against his employer and two railroads for personal injuries allegedly sustained in the course of interstate employment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Summary judgment of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California). The trial court had granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, an employer and two railroad companies, in the employee's action under the Federal Employers' Liability Act (FELA), 45 U.S.C.S. §§ 51-60.


OVERVIEW: An employee who worked for a company that maintained a fleet of refrigerator cars was injured while working inside a refrigerator car. The employee filed suit under FELA against his employer and the two railroad companies that owned 50 percent of the employer's corporate shares. The trial court granted a motion by the employer and the railroad companies for summary judgment and dismissed the case. The court affirmed. Granting summary judgment under California law was permissible in a FELA case; there was no incompatibility between the state summary judgment procedure and FELA. The employee did not have a cause of action under FELA because his employer was not a common carrier. The business of renting refrigeration cars and providing protective services was not the operation of a railroad as a means of carrying the public. The employee also did not actually work for the two railroad companies that owned his employer; the railroad companies did not exercise any control over the employer's operations or its employees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for an employer and two companies in an employee's action against them under FELA.

Santa Clara County Contractors & Homebuilders Asso. v. Santa Clara


Civ. No. 21887


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


232 Cal. App. 2d 564; 43 Cal. Rptr. 86; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1502



March 2, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 28, 1965. Burke, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Albert F. DeMarco, Judge.

Action seeking a declaration that city ordinance provisions, requiring payment of certain fees before approval of subdivision maps and issuance of building permits, are void and asking that defendants be enjoined from enforcing them.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which declared a city ordinance that required plaintiff association to pay certain fees before approval of subdivision maps and building permits would be granted, illegal and void.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that required payment of certain fees before approval of subdivision maps and the issuance of building permits would be granted. The association sued the city to void the ordinance. The association also sought an injunction to enjoin the city from enforcing the ordinance. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the association and declared the ordinance invalid. The city improperly attempted to use the Subdivision Map Act, Bus. & Prof. Code § 11500 et seq., for general revenue producing purposes. Moreover, the provisions of the city ordinance did not regulate the design and improvement of a subdivision, and because the state had preempted the field in all respects concerning subdivisions, except as to design and improvement, the ordinance was illegal and, therefore, void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the association and declared the city's ordinance illegal and void.

 

1363 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Patterson v. Municipal Court


Civ. No. 22285


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


232 Cal. App. 2d 289; 42 Cal. Rptr. 769; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1462



February 16, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Municipal Court for the San Jose-Milpitas-Alviso Judicial District of Santa Clara County, and Edward J. Nelson, Judge thereof, from proceeding with a prosecution for nonsupport of a minor child.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted prohibiting the court from taking the paternity issue from the jury and from instructing that an interlocutory divorce decree is res judicata on the paternity issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father challenged the decision of respondent Municipal Court for the San Jose-Milpitas-Alviso (California). Petitioner sought to restrain respondent from proceeding with prosecution of petitioner for violation of Cal. Penal Code § 270, for wilful failure to support a minor child.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that prohibition was a proper remedy because the possible denial of due process would have been an act in excess of jurisdiction and the constitutional application of a statute was being attacked. The court interpreted Cal. Penal Code § 270e to provide that a prima facie showing of paternity could have been made by a preponderance of the evidence. The court held that the proper application of § 270e required that if a showing of paternity appeared by a preponderance of the evidence defendant need merely to have gone forward with evidence to the extent of raising a reasonable doubt that he was the father. The court held that the trial court erred holding that the issue of paternity had to have been taken from the jury because the trial court determined that the judgment in the divorce action was res judicata of the issue of paternity. The court held that the interlocutory decree of divorce was admissible as evidence, but the issue of paternity had to be given the jury. The court held that defendant had been given an opportunity to meet the evidence and presumptions and in order to find him guilty the jury was required to find him so beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ, in favor of petitioner, prohibiting respondent from taking the paternity issue from the jury and from instructing that an interlocutory divorce decree was res judicata on the paternity issue.

People v. Ahmad


Crim. No. 4490


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


232 Cal. App. 2d 314; 42 Cal. Rptr. 854; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1464



February 16, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 9, 1965, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 14, 1965. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein. McComb, J., and Burke, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Leonard J. Dieden, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of conviction reversed solely on constitutional ground announced in People v. Dorado, 62 Cal.2d 338 [42 Cal.Rptr. 169, 398 P.2d 361].


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of her conviction by the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) for grand theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a payroll clerk. During her absence it was discovered that checks had been made to an employee known by no one. Defendant was questioned as to the identity of the employee and denied knowing the individual. Ultimately defendant was questioned by police at the department. Defendant confessed, and her confession was on tape, written out, and signed. The trial court convicted defendant of grand theft, and defendant appealed. The court determined that at the time of the confession the process had moved beyond investigation and into the realm of interrogation because defendant had become the focus of police attention. Defendant was made aware of neither her right to counsel nor her right to remain silent. The court reversed defendant's conviction on constitutional grounds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for grand theft.

West v. U. L. C. Corp.


Civ. No. 27552


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


232 Cal. App. 2d 85; 42 Cal. Rptr. 603; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1438



February 4, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County denying a motion to vacate and set aside default and default judgment. Leon T. David, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant assignee sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied its motion to vacate and set aside default and default judgment in plaintiff mortgagees' suit to declare the parties' rights in encumbered property.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagees, who held a second deed of trust on encumbered property, filed a suit against the assignee of the first deed of trust alleging that the assignee and the property owner had fraudulently reduced the value of the mortgagee's interest in the property. The trial court entered a default and default judgment against the assignee. On appeal, the assignee alleged that the commissioner of the trial court had no authority to enter the judgment against it or to reform its deed of trust. But the court affirmed the trial court's order after holding that the assignee's appeal had been timely filed. The court further held that the mortgagees had not been granted more relief than that for which they prayed because the reformation of the assignee's deed of trust was entailed in the relief that was prayed for in the complaint. The court also held that the commissioner had the power to decide the matter pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 259a. Finally, the court held that § 259a, which provided for court commissioners only in counties having a population of 900,000, was not unconstitutional because the congestion of such courts provided a reasonable basis for the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which denied the assignee's motion to vacate and set aside default and default judgment in the mortgagees' suit to declare the parties' rights in encumbered property.

Dumas v. Sunnyvale


Civ. No. 21338


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


231 Cal. App. 2d 796; 42 Cal. Rptr. 302; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1569



January 22, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. W. W. Jacka, Judge.

Action for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding validity of a street assessment district.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiffs reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which found in favor of plaintiff property owners in their action seeking to have the formation of an assessment district declared void and to enjoin the city and its agents from collecting any assessments under the district.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted a resolution to widen and improve a certain road and to create an assessment district to bear the cost of the resolution. The property owners filed protests, which were overruled by the city. The assessment district was formally inaugurated, and all of the property owners and non-party property owners within the district were ordered to pay assessments. The property owners filed suit challenging the creation of the district, and the trial court found in their favor. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by declaring the road project to be an improvement of city-wide benefit and that no special benefit was conferred upon the land within the district. The court reasoned that the trial court lacked authority to reweigh the evidence and to make its own findings on matters that the city was authorized to decide. The trial court also erred by declaring the entire district void and ordering the reimbursement of assessments paid by owners who were not parties to the action and not subject to the statute of limitations of Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 10400. Therefore, only the assessments levied against the party property owners were invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and directed the trial court to modify the judgment in accordance with the court's decision. The modified judgment was to provide, inter alia, that the assessment district was valid and that the assessments were invalid only as to the property owners who were plaintiffs in the action. The court further directed the trial court to remand the case to the city for reassessment proceedings.

 

1367 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Owens


Crim. No. 4579


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


231 Cal. App. 2d 691; 42 Cal. Rptr. 153; 1965 Cal. App. LEXIS 1555



January 14, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an alleged judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County and from an order suspending sentence and granting probation. Leonard J. Dieden, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft and for making false statements to obtain aid for needy children.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; appeal from alleged judgment dismissed. Order suspending sentence and granting probation affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants mother and stepfather sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which convicted them of grand theft involving the unlawful taking of money from the county. Additionally, the mother was charged with violating Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1550.


OVERVIEW: When the mother and stepfather were married, she had four children from a previous marriage. The former husband never complied with a child support order, and the mother received county aid. The mother was advised of stepfather liability procedures. The court found that county aid continued after the marriage because the mother and stepfather misrepresented his income. The mother and stepfather contended that the budgeting formula used to calculate eligibility for aid was invalid. The court found that the "stepfather liability" arrived at in any given month was never in excess of the mother's community property interest in the stepfather's income. The budgeting formula merely took the stepfather's income into consideration in determining the needs of his stepchildren. It neither deprived him of his income nor required him to support the children beyond the mother's community property interest in his income. The mother admitted that she knew the stepfather worked more hours than were indicated by the wage stubs that she reported. She admitted that she was required to report all his income. No other evidence was needed to support a finding of knowing misrepresentation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

DISPOSITION: Writ granted in part and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, City of Burbank and employees, sought to compel respondent, Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to set aside its order denying a motion to strike, overruling a demurrer, and denying a request to file an amended answer to a complaint filed by the real parties in interest, property owners, in a tort action against petitioners by the real parties in interest.


OVERVIEW: The real parties in interest, property owners, filed a tort action against petitioners, City of Burbank and employees. Gov't Code § 835.4(a), (b), contending that new public liability statutes determined the rights of the parties to the action. Respondent again rejected the motions, and petitioners sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent to strike the complaint and to grant leave to file the amended complaint.
