Petitioners should have had the opportunity to plead all defenses permitted by the statute, and the complaint had to be in proper form to enable them to do so.


OUTCOME: The court granted a writ of mandate directing respondent, Superior Court of Los Angeles County, to sustain petitioners', City of Burbank and employees, demurrer with leave to amend and to permit filing of an amended answer to permit all defenses permitted by the California Government Code. The real parties in interest could proceed against petitioners, so petitioners should have had the opportunity to plead all defenses permitted.

Santa Monica v. Superior Court of Los Angeles County


Civ. No. 28668


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


231 Cal. App. 2d 223; 41 Cal. Rptr. 824; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 799



December 15, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to compel the Superior Court of Los Angeles County to refrain from issuing an injunction restraining enforcement of certain city gambling ordinances.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city applied for a writ in prohibition to compel respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) from issuing an injunction in favor of real party in interest lounge operator that would restrain the city from enforcing certain gambling ordinances.


OVERVIEW: The lounge operator brought an action in the superior court that challenged city gambling ordinances. The lounger operator alleged that there were various constitutional challenges to gambling ordinances pending before the California Supreme Court and requested that the city be enjoined from enforcing the ordinances, claiming that it had no adequate remedy at law because the Supreme Court had not issued its own decision. After the superior court signaled its intent to issue a temporary injunction against the city, the city applied to the court for a writ of prohibition that would compel the superior court from issuing the injunction. Prior to the court's decision on the city's application, the Superior Court handed down a decision that rejected the general contention that municipal gambling ordinances were invalid. The court nonetheless issued a peremptory writ of prohibition, finding that the lounge operator had not claimed in support of its request for an injunction that it stood to suffer irreparable injury or any other sort of harm in the absence of an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of prohibition.

Emby Foods, Inc. v. Paul


Civ. No. 21749


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


230 Cal. App. 2d 687; 41 Cal. Rptr. 365; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 925



November 17, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 17, 1964, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 13, 1965. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Monroe Friedman, Judge.

Action to determine validity of an order of the Director of Agriculture setting minimum wholesale and retail prices for fluid milk and for a permanent injunction to prevent enforcement of such order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment upholding order affirmed; preliminary injunction dissolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retail grocers appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which found in favor of defendant director of agriculture (director) regarding the validity of the director's order setting minimum wholesale and retail prices for fluid milk. A preliminary injunction enjoining enforcement of the order was entered pending the resolution of the matter.


OVERVIEW: When the director issued an order that required that milk sold at a distributor's processing plant be four cents per gallon lower than the minimum retail store carry-out price, the retail grocers brought an action challenging the order as arbitrary and capricious. The complaint alleged that the new minimum prices were promulgated in violation of the applicable statutes without consideration of the relevant cost factors, were based on insufficient evidence, and were contrary to proper procedures. The trial court below found that there was substantial evidence in support of the minimum prices set by the order. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that, in light of the evidence presented at the hearing, the facts known to the director, and the director's duties under the Milk Stabilization Act, he could properly conclude that the combination of the elimination of the quantity discount together with the various price reductions ordered would not unduly harm the retail grocers, would encourage the orderly and efficient marketing of milk as to all methods of distribution, and would satisfy the statutory mandate of making milk available at the lowest price to consumers.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the preliminary injunction and affirmed the trial court's order upholding the director's order setting minimum prices for milk distributors.

People v. Madearos

Prosecution for operating a diesel truck in a manner resulting in the escape of excessive smoke.

Veh. Code § 27153.

The judgment of conviction was reversed by the appellate court, which then certified the cause to the court. The issue on appeal was whether § 27153 was unconstitutional in that the term "excessive smoke" was so indefinite as to render the statute impermissibly vague. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction because an ordinary and interested person would have had no difficulty in determining whether or not an excessive and unusual amount of smoke or offensive and excessive exhaust fumes accompanied the operation of a motor vehicle.

Flournoy v. State


Civ. No. 10876


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


230 Cal. App. 2d 520; 41 Cal. Rptr. 190; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 901



November 9, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 6, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Irving H. Perluss, Judge.

Action for wrongful death arising out of an accident caused by the allegedly dangerous and defective condition of a state highway.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to complaint was sustained without leave to amend reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff heirs appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) which sustained the State's demurrer without leave to amend their wrongful death complaint.


OVERVIEW: The complainants' cause of action against the state was based upon an alleged dangerous and defective condition of a highway. A moratorium legislation froze all pending litigation in which the doctrine of governmental immunity was an issue. After the development of the law of governmental tort liability, the State's demurrer was sustained because the complaint did not properly state a cause of action under the new law. The issues on appeal were: (1) whether the new legislation violated due process and equal protection, whether applied prospectively or retrospectively; (2) whether it was constitutional; (3) whether the complaint stated a cause of action under the new legislation; and (4) if not, could it have been amended to state one? After review, this court concluded that the legislation was constitutional; the complaint, although inadequately framed, could be amended to state a cause of action under the new legislation and under the common law of tort liability sans governmental immunity. The trial court erred prejudicially in sustaining the State's demurrer.


OUTCOME: The superior court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Buice


Crim. No. 9400


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


230 Cal. App. 2d 324; 40 Cal. Rptr. 877; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 876



October 21, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 17, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments (including orders granting probation) of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. David Coleman, Judge.

Prosecution for resisting executive officers in the performance of their duties, assault on peace officers with force likely to produce great bodily injury, and assault with intent to commit murder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to some defendants and affirmed in part and reversed in part as to other defendants. Judgments of conviction (including orders granting probation) of offenses charged and of simple assault affirmed; portions of certain judgments imposing double punishment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from judgments of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), convicting them of resisting executive officers in the performance of their duties, Cal. Penal Code § 69.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of resisting executive officers in the performance of their duties in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 69. Defendants appealed, arguing that the statute under which they were prosecuted was unconstitutionally vague. The court ruled that generally, the meaning of a statute must be definite and certain for it to be valid, and that this was particularly true of penal statutes defining offenses or prohibiting certain conduct. Further, the court held that all that was required pertaining to certainty was that the statute be reasonably certain and in accordance with the apparent purpose and intention of the legislature. The court affirmed the judgments convicting defendants, except to the extent of reversing certain sentences imposed, concluding that defendants could not urge that they did not know how many other kinds of executives could also be protected under Cal. Penal Code § 69 because the police officers involved clearly were within the group protected by the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgments convicting defendants were affirmed, except to the extent that certain sentences imposed on some defendants were reversed.

 

1374 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Perry


Crim. No. 4605


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


230 Cal. App. 2d 258; 40 Cal. Rptr. 829; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 867



October 19, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 17, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Harry J. Neubarth, Judge.

Prosecution for the improper use of a stolen credit card.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which convicted him of using a stolen credit card in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 484a(b)(6).


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the complaint had failed to charge a public offense or at most charged a misdemeanor and that he had been deprived of a substantial right because the trial court did not rule on his probation motion. The complaint alleged that defendant did knowingly and with intent to defraud use for the purpose of obtaining goods a credit card stolen from the possession of a cardholder, the value of such goods exceeding $ 50. The court rejected defendant's first claim, holding that § 484a(b)(6) did not require that the credit card be stolen by the person charged or that it be stolen in California. It was sufficient if defendant knowingly had wrongful possession and used the card for the purposes indicated in the statute. If the complaint was ambiguous in charging that defendant actually obtained over $ 50 worth of goods, the ambiguity should have been raised in the trial court and could not be considered on appeal. Further, defendant was not deprived of a substantial right when the trial court failed to rule on his probation motion. The trial court properly concluded that he was ineligible for probation and it had no choice but to sentence him to an appropriate institution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1375 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Calnev Pipe Line Co. v. Colton


Civ. No. 7177


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


230 Cal. App. 2d 184; 40 Cal. Rptr. 755; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 861



October 16, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 9, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Carl B. Hilliard, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a city and its council to cease annexation proceedings and to restrain its clerk from filing a certified copy of an annexation ordinance or in certiorari to review annexation proceedings.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ of mandate affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which denied a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, a city and its city council, to cease annexation proceedings and to restrain the city clerk from filing a certified copy of an annexation ordinance or, in certiorari, to review the annexation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The property owner alleged that it was denied a fair hearing before the city council and that the protest statute, Cal. Gov't Code § 35313, was unconstitutional as applied to the disputed facts. On appeal, the court affirmed the superior court's judgment. The property owner was not denied a fair hearing because the city council complied with § 35313 by determining that the protestors accounted for less than half of the total assessed value of the land to be annexed. The protestors owned only 8.07 percent of the value of the land to be annexed, and there was no evidence that the city council acted impartially. Application of § 35313 was not unconstitutional because the annexation did not operate as a taking without due process, as alleged by the property owner. Annexation proceedings were not based on a city's police power, which was restricted to the city's limits. The legislature derived authority to provide for annexation from Cal. Const. art. XI, § 6, and the mode adopted was, therefore, a question of policy and expediency. Because no one had a vested right to be included or excluded from a local governmental unit, the annexation did not invade any constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

 

1376 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Ferreira v. Barham


Civ. No. 10833


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


230 Cal. App. 2d 128; 40 Cal. Rptr. 739; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 854



October 14, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 9, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Glenn County. Wright L. Callender, Judge.

Action by a guest for personal injuries arising out of an accident in which an automobile left the road and rolled on its side.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of nonsuit affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, guest and associated individuals, sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Glenn County (California), which rendered a nonsuit in appellants' action for personal injuries arising out of an accident in which an automobile left the road and rolled on its side.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that Cal. Veh. Code § 17158, the guest statute, violated due process and equal protection. The court stated that effectually, appellants would have frozen common law principles. However, society was not static; society was fluid; and society was also complex with the complexities modernly increasing, particularly in the matter of automobile traffic, in geometric progression. Therefore, the law, both statutory and common law, must have kept pace. Hence the statutory changes in common law rules by the legislature made as a matter of state policy to meet current needs and upheld by the courts as a proper exercise of the police power within the limitations enunciated were not in violation of the human rights of free men; not violation of due process; not a denial of equal protection. The court affirmed the judgment rendering a nonsuit in appellants' action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment, which entered a nonsuit in appellants' action for personal injuries arising out of an accident.

 

1377 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


Crim. No. 9541


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


230 Cal. App. 2d 80; 40 Cal. Rptr. 711; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 848



October 7, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment (order granting probation) of the Superior Court of Ventura County and from an order denying a new trial. Louis C. Drapeau, Judge. *


* Retired Justice of the District Court of Appeal sitting under assignment by the Chairman of the Judicial Council.

Prosecution for felony drunk driving.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, appeal from order dismissed. Judgment (order granting probation following conviction) affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California) granting probation on defendant's conviction for felony drunk driving in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23101.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction and that the trial court drew the wrong inferences from the uncontradicted facts. Defendant also argued that both Cal. Veh. Code § 23101 and the pleading, which was in the words of § 23101, were lacking in the specific detail necessary to apprise him of the conduct that was forbidden. The criticism of § 23101 was that it referred to "any act forbidden by law in the driving of a vehicle." Defendant argued that § 23101 was defective in that it failed to specify the acts which were forbidden. The court found that it could not say that the trial court could not reasonably have inferred that defendant was driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor within the meaning of § 23101. The information charged the offense in the words of § 23101, thus complying with Cal. Penal Code § 952. The language in § 23101 did not have a variety of meanings in common usage and it did not lack precision. Every operator of a motor vehicle was required to know what acts were forbidden by law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting probation.

 

1378 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


McConnell v. All-Coverage Ins. Exchange Auto. & Fire


Civ. Nos. 27739, 27740


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


229 Cal. App. 2d 735; 40 Cal. Rptr. 587; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1040



September 16, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 14, 1964, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Above. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 10, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County awarding attorneys' and auditors' fees and advances against costs pending a hearing on the merits of a conservatorship proceeding initiated by the Insurance Commissioner. Alfred Gitelson and Philip H. Richards, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Motion to augment record denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance commissioner sought review of the orders of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which awarded attorneys' and auditors' fees and advances against costs pending a hearing on the merits of a conservatorship proceeding initiated by the commissioner pursuant to Cal. Ins. Code §1011.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner filed an application pursuant to § 1011 in the trial court for an order appointing a conservator in light of the condition of respondents, an insurer and its underwriter. On appeal, the commissioner argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to award attorneys' fees, expenses, or costs from the insurer and its underwriter's assets in a conservator proceeding. The commissioner contended that a § 1011 proceeding was a special proceeding, the court having only those powers that were expressly granted to it by statute. The court disagreed, and affirmed. The court held that once the commissioner assumed the duty of appointing a conservator, he was subject to the jurisdiction of the court to the same extent as were all receivers of corporations. The court found that to hold that the trial court lacked jurisdiction would have been to countenance a de facto deprivation of property without due process of law. The court found that the fact that the commissioner's position was ultimately sustained did not mean that the insurer's attempt to defend was in bad faith. The court denied the commissioner's request to augment the record by inclusion of subsequent proceedings.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1379 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Burk v. Municipal Court for Whittier Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 28033


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


229 Cal. App. 2d 696; 40 Cal. Rptr. 425; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1035



September 15, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. A. Curtis Smith, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to enjoin a municipal court from prosecuting petitioners for violating allegedly invalid zoning ordinance prohibiting commercial signs in residential zones.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner realtors appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denying their writ of prohibition against further prosecution for violations of an allegedly invalid zoning ordinance prohibiting commercial signs in residential zones. The realtors contended that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The realtors filed an action, seeking a writ of prohibition enjoining respondent trial court from prosecuting them for violating a municipal ordinance that prohibited all commercial signs in a residential area. The trial court denied their writ and they appealed, asserting that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, ruling that the ordinance was a valid and lawful exercise of the police power. It held that the municipal ordinance was constitutional. The exceptions permitted under the ordinance were reasonable and nondiscriminatory. Permitting a name or identification sign of limited size applied equally to all. Permitting the property owner to erect a sign of limited size advertising the leasing, rental, or sale of the property was proper so as not to unduly restrict the renting or sale of property. The prohibition against "for rent" or "for sale" signs by real estate brokers, with the name of their realty companies was a reasonable restriction regulating advertising. Whether or not such incidental commercial advertising merited the signs' exclusion, was for the sound discretion of the legislative body and not the reviewing court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the realtors' writ of prohibition to enjoin their prosecution for violation of a municipal ordinance restricting the erection of commercial signs in a residential neighborhood.

 

1380 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Huddleson


Crim. Nos. 4488, 4602


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


229 Cal. App. 2d 618; 40 Cal. Rptr. 581; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1025



September 14, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions of all the Respondents for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied November 10, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco granting a writ of habeas corpus and discharging respondent in No. 4488 from custody after conviction of loitering about a public place at or near which children attend and normally congregate and from an order of the Municipal Court for the City and County of San Francisco dismissing complaints filed against defendants in No. 4602 for the same offense after sustaining demurrers to complaints with leave to amend and plaintiff failed to amend. Francis McCarty (Crim. No. 4488) and Clayton W. Horn (Crim. No. 4602), Judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which granted petitioner convict a writ of habeas corpus and in a separate case upheld Cal. Penal Code ))) 647(a)(2) and reversed a judgment of the trial court that dismissed defendants' charges for loitering.


OVERVIEW: The convict filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus after he was convicted of loitering, which the lower court granted on the grounds that ))) 647(a)(2) was vague and indefinite and therefore unlawful. Defendants' charges for loitering were dismissed by the trial court for the same reason and on appeal the case was transferred to the court to determine the constitutionality of ))) 647(a)(2). The convict appealed. In reversing and remanding the trial court's judgments regarding the convict and defendants, the court held that the trial court erred. The court found that the term loiter had a clear and reasonable definite significance in the context of ))) 647(a)(2) and that it was not vague, did not violate constitutional rights, or interfere with personal rights and liberties. The court concluded that the loitering condemned by ))) 647(a)(2) was that of lingering about public schools for a sinister purpose, which it determined the convict was correctly found guilty of and defendants were correctly charged with.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1381 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hurd v. Paquin


Civ. No. 28110


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


229 Cal. App. 2d 634; 40 Cal. Rptr. 524; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1027



September 14, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 10, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Frank C. Charvat, Judge.

Action for damages for false imprisonment and for assault and battery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in favor of defendant police officers under Long Beach, Calif., Municipal Code §§ 2710-2710.6, in a suit for false imprisonment, assault, and battery.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff appealed a judgment in favor of the police officers under a municipal ordinance that required suits against police officers to be filed pursuant to a specified claim procedure. Plaintiff sought recovery for damages based on the police officers' alleged false imprisonment, battery, and assault. The court observed that although the complaint did not allege that the police officers were engaged in the course of their employment, he did stipulate during pretrial that the police officers were "duly appointed officers" and such stipulation superseded the issues raised by the pleadings. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the lower court properly concluded that plaintiff's failure to comply with the city ordinance's condition precedent to the filing of the action was fatal to the maintenance of the action. The court rejected plaintiff's claim that the ordinance was unconstitutional because the state had preempted the field. The court reasoned that the absence of state preemption was demonstrated by the fact that the existing jurisdiction of cities to govern matters by charter with regard to claims against public employees was recognized in Cal. Govt. Code § 730.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the police officers on plaintiff's intentional tort claims.

 

1382 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Galyon v. Municipal Court for San Bernardino Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 7357


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


229 Cal. App. 2d 667; 40 Cal. Rptr. 446; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1032



September 14, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Archie D. Mitchell, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain the Municipal Court for the San Bernardino Judicial District of San Bernardino County from trying plaintiff on a criminal complaint.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), denying his application for a writ of prohibition seeking to restrain respondent municipal court from trying the father on a criminal complaint for exhibiting his Siamese twin sons for hire, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 400.


OVERVIEW: The father was charged with exhibiting his Siamese twin sons for an admission fee. On appeal from the denial of his application for writ of prohibition, the father argued that § 400 was unconstitutional and void. The court reversed. The court found that under § 400, the act of exhibiting a deformity was not immoral, or injurious to the health of the people, or against the public welfare. The prohibition was to anyone making a financial transaction out of the exhibiting of the deformity. The court held that the financial transaction was not immoral, dangerous to general health, or against public welfare of the people. While the reasonable objective of the statute upon its enactment may have been a valid exercise of the police power because of the changed conditions during the intervening 91 years there was no reasonable objective to be reached by the statute. That there might be regulation of exhibits of abnormalities was not questioned, but the court concluded that the prohibition of them was an improper exercise of the police power of the state when superimposed upon public morals and welfare of the present era.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and ordered that the superior court issue the writ of prohibition.

 

1383 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hanks v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 27977


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


229 Cal. App. 2d 427; 40 Cal. Rptr. 478; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1002



August 31, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 28, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Steven S. Weisman, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the State Board of Equalization to increase assessment rolls of all counties of the state to make them conform to full cash value.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found that the process of respondent State Board of Equalization of assessing property by the use of its full cash value as a standard and applying a common ratio to full cash value of the property did not violate constitutional or statutory provisions dealing with assessments of property.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought a proceeding in mandamus to compel the Board to increase assessment rolls to make them conform to full cash value. The trial court found that the process of using full cash value as a base and applying a ratio to full cash value in order to arrived at assessed value did not violate any constitutional or statutory provisions, and the court affirmed. It found that the only expressed constitutional duty of the Board was to equalize the valuation of taxable property in the counties of the state and that neither the duty nor the Board's power to increase or lower the assessment roll so as to equalize the assessment and make it conform to the true value of the property contained in the roll was set in terms of equalizing at 100 percent of market value. Further, Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 9, was intended to permit the Board to equalize on the basis of fractional assessments to full cash value because, if it was intended that all property was to be assessed at 100 percent of market value, the Board would not need the power to make the rolls or assessments conform to cash value as it would be bound by the 100 percent requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied the taxpayer a writ of mandamus to compel the Board to increase assessment rolls to make them to conform to full cash value of the property.

Walters v. Contractors' State License Board


Civ. No. 28017


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


229 Cal. App. 2d 449; 40 Cal. Rptr. 390; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1004



August 31, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 22, 1964, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 28, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred Gitelson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to nullify an administrative order denying a contractor's license.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ and discharging alternative writ, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electrical contractor challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied his application for a writ of mandate to nullify respondent Contractors' State License Board's order that denied him a contractor's license.


OVERVIEW: The contractor filed his license application on March 14, 1963, and the registrar of contractors (registrar) adopted the proposed order of the hearing officer on April 17, 1963, and the decision to deny the contractor's request became effective on May 14, 1963. The contractor received the decision on May 6, 1963, and he wrote the office of administrative procedure requesting the cost of a transcript from the hearing. After receiving a cost estimate and paying the fee, the contractor received the completed record on June 18, 1963. The contractor's application was filed on July 2, 1963 after the clerk initially rejected it. On August 5, 1963, a return was made to the writ and the affirmative defense of the time limitations for filing the application for the writ was pleaded. The registrar argued that the contractor's application for writ of mandate expired on June 13, 1963, 30 days after the order became effective. The court found that under Cal. Gov't Code § 11523, because the contractor received the registrar's decision on May 6 he had until July 5 to file his application for writ of mandate. The contractor was not required to seek reconsideration under Cal. Gov't Code § 11521.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the contractor's application for writ of mandate. The case was remanded for trial on issues other than the timeliness of the contractor's application.

 

1385 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Hart


Crim. No. 9250


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


229 Cal. App. 2d 455; 40 Cal. Rptr. 420; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1005



August 31, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 17, 1964, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 28, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein. Traynor, C. J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County granting a writ of habeas corpus in an extradition proceeding. E. Perry Churchill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which granted a writ of habeas corpus in an extradition proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Respondent individual had filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus. He argued that the Governor's warrant, pursuant to which he was arrested and the papers accompanying the same, affirmatively indicated on their face that there had been no compliance with the requirements of Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1661. After a hearing on the matter, the petition was granted. The primary issue on appeal was whether § 1661(b) created a mandatory condition precedent before the Governor of California could honor a request for extradition of a person, not a "fugitive" within the meaning of U.S. Const. art. IV, for his failure to support dependents in the demanding state. The court believed it did. The court held that the provision in Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1661(b), requiring the Governor to call upon any prosecutor to investigate the demand for extradition, was a mandatory condition precedent before the Governor could decide to honor the request for extradition. Absent compliance with the requirement of § 1661(b), the Governor was without jurisdiction to issue a warrant for a nonfugitive on a nonsupport charge. The warrant was void and afforded no authority for detention of the individual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order.

 

1386 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Michels v. Watson


Civ. No. 27835


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


229 Cal. App. 2d 404; 40 Cal. Rptr. 464; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1001



August 31, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 28, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Steven S. Weisman, Judge.

Action by a taxpayer for declaratory relief to compel a county assessor to assess property at full cash value.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which declared that Cal. Const. art. XI, § 12, did not prohibit respondent tax assessor from assessing taxable property by a county at a uniform fraction of its full cash value. The taxpayer sought to compel the tax assessor to assess property at full cash value in his action for declaratory relief.


OVERVIEW: The tax assessor announced his intention to assess all property in the county at 25 percent of its fair market value and the taxpayer filed his declaratory judgment action. On appeal from a judgment in favor of the tax assessor, the sole issue before the court was whether locally assessable tangible property could be legally assessed at a uniform fraction of its full cash value. The court ruled that it could and affirmed the judgment. The court analyzed pertinent statutes and constitutional provisions. Although Cal. Const. art. XI, § 12 and Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 401 specifically stated that property was to be assessed at its full cash value, the court ruled that the administrative construction resulting in the assessment of taxable property by a county at a uniform fraction of its full cash value was not erroneous or unauthorized. The practice of assessing at a uniform fraction of full cash value on a standard of full cash value had been consistently followed since 1872 with the knowledge and permission of both the California Legislature and the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the tax assessor in the taxpayer's action for a declaratory judgment prohibiting the tax assessor from assessing property at a uniform fraction of its cash value.

Savelli v. Board of Medical Examiners


Civ. No. 21492


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


229 Cal. App. 2d 124; 40 Cal. Rptr. 171; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 967



August 13, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 4, 1964, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 7, 1964. Mosk, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Byron Arnold, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Board of Medical Examiners to permit plaintiff to take the written examination for a license as a physician and surgeon.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical student sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied the medical student's writ of mandate to compel respondent board of medical examiners to permit the medical student to take the written examination for a license as a physician and surgeon.


OVERVIEW: The medical student filed an application with the board of medical examiners for an examination for a physician's and surgeon's certificate. The application was denied on the ground that the medical student was not a graduate of a medical school approved by the board of medical examiners. The medical student requested a hearing before the board of medical examiners, and a hearing was had before a hearing officer. The board of medical examiners denied the application on the ground that the medical student was not able to present evidence that he had complied with the requirements of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2290. The medical student sought judicial review and filed a petition for writ of mandate in the trial court. The trial court ruled for the board of medical examiners, holding that the medical student was not entitled to a writ of mandate. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the board of medical examiners provided substantial evidence to support their conclusion that the medical school the medical student graduated from did not meet the requirements of § 2290 and that the medical student failed to sustain his burden to prove compliance with the requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the medical student's writ of mandate to compel the board of medical examiners to permit the medical student to take the written examination.

 

1388 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Phillis v. Santa Barbara


Civ. No. 27834


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


229 Cal. App. 2d 45; 40 Cal. Rptr. 27; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 959



August 6, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied September 3, 1964, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 7, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County. John A. Westwick, Judge.

Action to determine pension rights of a former policeman and a former fireman under a city charter.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to second amended complaint was sustained with leave to amend and plaintiffs declined to amend, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, ex-policeman and ex-fireman, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Barbara (California), which held that their declaratory actions regarding their pension rights were barred by Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 338(1). Plaintiffs alleged that defendant city was estopped from relying upon the defense of limitation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, ex-policeman and ex-fireman, filed declaratory actions against defendant city for a determination of their pension rights under a city charter. The actions arose out of a charter amendment that substituted a fixed period for a fluctuating one and imposed a minimum age requirement. Defendant filed a demurer alleging plaintiffs' actions were barred by Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 338(1). The trial court sustained the demurer and subsequently entered a take nothing judgment against plaintiffs. Upon review, the court reversed. The court held that plaintiffs' claims seeking declaratory relief were not barred by the statute of limitations where defendant was equitably estopped from asserting the defense of limitation because city officials had misled plaintiffs as to their pension rights. The court noted the officials that had misled plaintiffs stood in confidential relationships to plaintiffs and had asserted that they were fully informed of the law. The court determined the charter amendment was invalid as applied to plaintiffs because it imposed burdensome limitations upon pension rights that were unaccompanied by compensating benefits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that held declaratory actions filed by plaintiffs, ex-policeman and ex-fireman, were barred by the statute of limitations. The court held that the declaratory actions were not barred by the statute of limitations where defendant was equitably estopped from asserting the defense of limitation because city officials had misled plaintiffs as to their pension rights under a city charter.

Guardianship of Hicks


Civ. No. 21264


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


228 Cal. App. 2d 629; 39 Cal. Rptr. 698; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1122



July 23, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from part of an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco in guardianship proceedings which denied an equitable lien on the property of an incompetent person for the entire amount of charges made for her care at a state mental hospital. T. I. Fitzpatrick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to payments allowed and reversed with directions as to denial of equitable lien.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Mental Hygiene sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which ordered appellee guardian to make monthly payments for the care of an incompetent person and which denied an equitable lien on the property of the incompetent person for the entire amount of charges made for her care at a state mental hospital.


OVERVIEW: The Department sought payment for the care of the incompetent person. The trial court ordered that the guardian make a monthly payment but denied its request for an equitable lien on the property of the incompetent person for the entire amount of charges made for her care at a state mental hospital. The Department appealed. The court affirmed as to the monthly payment and reversed as to the denial of the equitable lien. The court found that the liability of the estate of the incompetent for the charges made for her care at the state hospital was a statutory one and unconditional. The court held that there was no basis for denial of the lien. There was no reason why the Department should not have been reimbursed to the extent of the estate for a balance incurred for her care. The trial court had protected the incompetent during her lifetime, and the court held that there was no reason, on the other hand, why the state should not have been protected as to the additional amount charged by imposition of a lien.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the payments required by the trial court and reversed the denial of the equitable lien.

 

1390 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hope v. Contractors' State License Board


Civ. No. 10755


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


228 Cal. App. 2d 414; 39 Cal. Rptr. 514; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1096



July 10, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 2, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Butte County. Jean Morony, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Contractors' State License Board and the Registrar of Contractors to reinstate plaintiff's contractor's license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Butte County (California), which denied the contractor's writ of mandate commanding respondent board to reinstate his contractor's license.


OVERVIEW: The contractor's license was revoked after a hearing on an accusation charging him with violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 7113.5. Under § 7113.5 adjudication and acts of bankruptcy were cause for disciplinary action. The contractor petitioned the superior court for a writ of mandate commanding respondent board to reinstate him, which was denied. The contractor appealed and the court affirmed the judgment of the superior court. The court answered the contractor's contention that the vesting of discretion in the registrar constituted an invalid delegation of powers by reassertion of the rule that although the legislature cannot confer unlimited power upon an administrative officer without designating standards to guide the officer's action, it nevertheless need not lay down minutely defined standards. The court held that the provisions of § 7113.5 vesting in the registrar the authority to consider acts of bankruptcy as a cause of disciplinary action, which action could extend to the revocation of a license, was a valid exercise of the state's police power and was not in conflict with the federal Bankruptcy Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that denied the contractor's writ of mandate commanding the board to reinstate him.

 

1391 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Boyd v. Boyd


Civ. No. 10759


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


228 Cal. App. 2d 374; 39 Cal. Rptr. 400; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1092



July 8, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 30, 1964. Pierce, P. J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 2, 1964. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Plumas County. Ben V. Curler, Judge.

Action for damages for breach of an express oral promise to live with and support plaintiff, for fraudulently making promises to live with and support her without any intention of fulfilling these promises and for negligently marrying her or negligently leaving her without reasonable care as to her support.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to complaint was sustained with leave to amend and plaintiff failed to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife brought an action against defendant husband for breach of an express oral promise to live with and support her, for fraudulently making promises to live with and support her without intention of fulfilling the promise, and for negligently leaving her without reasonable care as to her support. The Superior Court of Plumas County (California) sustained the husband's general demurrer, and the wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband contended that his wife's claims were barred under Cal. Civ. Code §§ 43.4, 43.5. The court found that the occurrence of a marriage ceremony did not affect the operation of the §§ 43.4 and 43.5, as the breach occurred whether by postnuptial or antenuptial renunciation. The court found that the legislature's amendment to the law made the provision of the statutes that barred this sort of action apply to postnuptial breaches. The court found that breach of promise actions were aimed at financial vindication of the entire group of marital expectations and commitments and frustrated economic expectations that did not escape § 43.5. The court found that the wife had available alternative remedies to recoup her loss and to allow recovery could permit her to receive duplicate recoveries. Thus, the wife's claim of special damages was barred under § 43.5(d). As to the claim of fraud in promising to live with and support the wife, the court found that its objective was an action for damages, not restitution and fell under § 43.4. The negligence claim likewise fell under the statute because it was a transparent pleading device to circumvent a statutory barrier.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1392 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. De Young


Crim. No. 9956


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


228 Cal. App. 2d 331; 39 Cal. Rptr. 487; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1086



July 6, 1964 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court for the Santa Barbara Judicial District of Santa Barbara County. Frank P. Kearney, Judge.

Prosecution for wilfully appearing on private premises in a state of intoxication to the annoyance of another person.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to the criminal complaint was sustained, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People sought review of an order of the Municipal Court for the Santa Barbara Judicial District of Santa Barbara County (California), sustaining defendant's demurrer and dismissing the People's complaint that defendant willfully appeared on private premises in a state of intoxication to the annoyance of another person in violation of Santa Barbara, Cal., City Code § 32.11.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with the lower court that City Code § 32.11 was invalid because the state adopted a general scheme for the regulation of the criminal aspects of being intoxicated. The numerous legislative enactments regulating the criminal aspects of intoxication, and particularly in view of the language of Cal. Penal Code § 647(f), taken with the circumstances of its enactment and the decisions of the California Supreme Court, the legislature determined by implication that it intended to preempt the field for the regulation of the criminal aspects of being intoxicated, both in public and private places.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sustaining of the demurrer and dismissal of the prosecution for willfully appearing on private premises in a state of intoxication to the annoyance of another person.

 

1393 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Duarte


Civ. No. 27519


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


228 Cal. App. 2d 267; 39 Cal. Rptr. 524; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1078



June 30, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 27, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Charles R. Thompson, Judge.

Action to enjoin enforcement of an allegedly unconstitutional zoning ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal without prejudice affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners filed an action challenging the ordinance of appellee town. The property owners sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that entered judgment in favor of the town.


OVERVIEW: The matter before the court concerned an action to enjoin enforcement of an allegedly unconstitutional zoning ordinance. The trial court dismissed the action for lack of jurisdiction. The property owners contended that the new setbacks were similar to the requirements that had been repealed therefore the new ordinance was unconstitutional. The property owners did not avail themselves of the administrative remedies that were available prior to commencing litigation. The court determined that the property owners were without standing to challenge the validity of the ordinance until they exhausted the administrative remedy available to them. The court held that there was no justifiable reason why the doctrine of exhaustion of administrative remedies did not apply to the property owners' case. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered against the property owners.

 

1394 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Frey


Crim. No. 9012


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


228 Cal. App. 2d 33; 39 Cal. Rptr. 49; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1057



June 19, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 30, 1964, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 12, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment (order granting probation) of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Donald R. Wright, Judge.

Prosecution for pimping, pandering and conspiracy to commit these offenses.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Order granting probation affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions for pimping under Cal. Penal Code § 266h, pandering under Cal. Penal Code § 266i, and conspiracy to commit pimping and pandering under Cal. Penal Code § 182 by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California).


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned a hotel in which he received earnings from prostitutes. Defendant claimed that he merely rented rooms to prostitutes and there was insufficient evidence to prove otherwise. The court affirmed the convictions for pimping, pandering, and conspiracy to commit pimping and pandering based on sufficient evidence and corroborating testimony. The court held that one prostitute was not an accomplice and therefore, her testimony was properly corroborating. The jury instructions were proper, clear, consistent with the criminal statutes, and not misleading. There was also sufficient proof of the pandering conviction because defendant not only rented rooms to prostitutes, but he and his business associate procured women to live at the hotel as prostitutes. A witness' testimony was admissible though she had changed her testimony to an unsworn statement because she thought that defendant had attempted to frame her for crimes that she did not commit. The unsworn statement did not have to be accepted as fact. Due to a lack of objection and prejudice, the jury instructions were proper. Evidence in plain sight in defendant's hotel room was properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for pimping, pandering, and conspiracy to pimp and to pander.

 

1395 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board


Civ. No. 27792


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


228 Cal. App. 2d 1; 39 Cal. Rptr. 192; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1053



June 17, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 29, 1964, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 12, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Alfred Gitelson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board to set aside its decision reversing a decision of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control denying an application for an on-sale beer and wine license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Director of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which affirmed the decision of respondent Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board, which had reversed the department's decision to not grant an on sale beer and wine license to respondent bar owner.


OVERVIEW: The bar owner submitted an application to the department for an on sale beer and wine license, but it was denied. The board reversed the department's decision so the department appealed, and the trial court affirmed the decision of the board. The department then appealed to the court, which again affirmed the decision of the board. The court found there was a legal conflict between Cal. Penal Code § 172 and Cal. Code Regs. tit. 4, § 61.1 (1959), and that § 61.1 was unconstitutional and void. The court held that the bar owner's premises was a bona fide public eating place and, unless good cause, other than proximity or student patronage, existed, it could not be contended that such premise was not entitled to be licensed. The court ruled that Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22(5) gave the department the exclusive power to license except as provided and in accordance with laws enacted by the legislature. The court found that under Cal. Penal Code § 172, the legislature removed restrictions imposed on bona fide public eating places. The department could not impose restrictions, which nullified the effect of the legislative enactment. Such restrictions constituted an arrogation of authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had affirmed the board's decision reversing the department's decision that the bar owner was not entitled to an on sale beer and wine license.

 

1396 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Keeler Street Development Co. v. Department of Invest., Div. of Corps.


Civ. No. 21365


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


227 Cal. App. 2d 760; 39 Cal. Rptr. 44; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1231



June 12, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 9, 1964, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 5, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Byron Arnold, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Department of Investment of the Division of Corporations to set aside its order denying a permit to make effective an amendment to articles of incorporation making previously nonassessable shares of corporate stock assessable and to withdraw its notice of hearing or to issue its permit; and action for a judgment declaring certain provisions of the Corporations Code to be unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), affirming the decision of the Commissioner of Corporations on behalf of respondent prohibiting the change of non-assessable stocks to assessable.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation held a stockholders meeting where it amended its articles of incorporation to allow certain shares of stock to become assessable. The minority stockholders protested, arguing that the change needed to be approved by respondent Commissioner of Corporations. Respondent agreed with the minority stockholders, finding substantial evidence did not show a necessity for making shares assessable, and refused to grant them a permit. Appellant filed a writ of mandate to have respondent set aside its order and to issue a permit as well as for declaratory judgment finding several provisions of the Corporate Code to be unconstitutional. The trial court discharged the writ, upheld the findings of fact adopted by respondent, and ordered appellant take nothing. The appellate court affirmed and concluded the rights of shareholders would be changed if appellant was allowed to convert non-assessable stock to assessable, and the permit was needed for securities already issued.


OUTCOME: The lower court's judgment was affirmed because appellant needed a permit to convert non-assessable stock to assessable even though the stocks were already issued.

 

1397 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Coronado v. San Diego Unified Port Dist.


Civ. No. 7416


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


227 Cal. App. 2d 455; 38 Cal. Rptr. 834; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1204



May 26, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 22, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. A. Curtis Smith, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to enjoin operation of a port district; and to determine rights and duties of a city under a statutory grant in trust of tidelands, legality of procedures employed in establishing the district, power of the state to revoke the trust, and constitutionality of voting procedures established under the act providing for formation of the district.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrers to complaint were sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, city, and individual taxpayer, appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which dismissed all counts of plaintiffs' complaint in an action to enjoin the formal establishment of the district after sustaining defendants, registrar of voter's, and supervisors of the county and state's, general demurrers without leave to amend.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, city, and individual taxpayer, appealed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed all counts of plaintiffs' complaint in an action to enjoin the formal establishment of the unified port district, after sustaining defendants, registrar of voter's, and supervisors of the county and state's, general demurrers without leave to amend. The trial court's judgment of dismissal and sustaining of the demurrers were affirmed. The court held that the causes of action in the complaint could not be amended to state a cause of action and the demurrers were properly sustained without leave to amend. Further, appellants had no right to challenge the validity of the formation of the district. The Due Process Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, afforded no immunity against mere inequalities in tax burdens, nor did it afford protection against their increase as an indirect consequence of a state's exercise of its political powers. Appellant was not denied equal protection because a citizen of one municipality was not deprived of property without due process of law by being subjected to increased tax burdens as a result of the consolidation of his city with another.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of dismissal after demurrers to plaintiffs' complaint were sustained without leave to amend because the Due Process Clause afforded no immunity against mere inequalities in tax burdens, nor did it afford protection against their increase as an indirect consequence of a state's exercise of its political powers.

 

1398 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Stadler v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 27631


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


227 Cal. App. 2d 314; 38 Cal. Rptr. 587; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1186



May 19, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 5, 1964, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 15, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. A. Curtis Smith, Judge.

Action to recover motor vehicle transportation license tax paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a participating carrier involved in the interstate shipment of goods under a division agreement, paid a motor vehicle transportation tax, exhausted his administrative remedies, and instituted an action to recover the taxes. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered judgment for defendant, the State Board of Equalization (California). The carrier appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under the division agreement, participating carriers shipped goods origin-to-destination as single through shipments but physically handled shipments as "joint through movement" by two or more carriers acting under an "interline" arrangement. Carriers operating under the division agreement received a greater proportion of the total freight charges than that which a mileage proration would have produced because they incurred extra costs for handling. The Board treated the full amount of the carrier's proportion of the freight charges as "gross receipts" under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 9606 and did not apply a mileage proration. On appeal from the Board's judgment, the court held that the carrier was not entitled to a refund because the taxing of "transportation operations" under § 9606 included any and all activities that contributed to an origin-to-destination movement. Because all of the carrier's mileage was in California, the Board treated as "gross receipts" all of the compensation that was allocated to the carrier. The carrier was not exempt from taxation under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 9653(b) because none of its shipments remained entirely within any incorporated city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1399 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Lawing v. Faull


Civ. No. 28140


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


227 Cal. App. 2d 23; 38 Cal. Rptr. 417; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1152



April 30, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 24, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to compel the mayor and other city officials to call a municipal referendum election in connection with a rezoning ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Order to show cause discharged and writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer requested a writ of mandamus, seeking to compel respondent city clerk to certify the sufficiency of a referendum petition concerning a rezoning ordinance, and to compel respondents, mayor and city council, to call an election upon the referendum.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed a referendum petition with the city clerk. The city clerk refused to certify the petition because it failed to comply with the signature requirements of 1911 Cal. Stat. § 143, which required that the petition be signed by at least 20 percent of the total number of registered voters. The taxpayer filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the city council to call an election. The court denied the petition, holding that § 143 was not subordinated to Cal. Const. art. IV, § 1, and art. XI, §§ 6, 8. Article IV, § 1, provided that not more than 15 percent of the electors were needed to propose any initiative measure, and that not more than 10 percent were needed for the referendum. The court construed the language of art. IV, § 1, as not curtailing the powers of those cities having charters. However, art. IV, § 1, placed a restriction on the city to refrain from withholding the initiative and referendum powers reserved by the constitution. The court held that the limitation did not extend to include the provisions concerning the percentage of voters required.


OUTCOME: The court denied the taxpayer's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the city clerk to certify the referendum petition and to compel the city council to call an election.

 

1400 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Aday


Crim. No. 4101


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


226 Cal. App. 2d 520; 38 Cal. Rptr. 199; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1306



April 21, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied May 15, 1964, and Respondents' Petitions for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied June 16, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Alameda County setting aside an indictment. Donald K. Quayle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) that set aside an indictment against defendants under Cal. Penal Code § 995 on the ground that defendants were indicted without reasonable or probable cause. Defendants were charged under Cal. Penal Code § 182 with conspiracy to write, publish, or distribute obscene materials in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 311.


OVERVIEW: A writ was granted directing the superior court to return all of the defendants' seized property except two books which had been specifically named in the affidavit for an allegedly invalid search warrant and in the warrant itself. The majority of the exhibits which were before the grand jury were withdrawn, and the superior court set aside the indictment. The court examined the remaining evidence received by the grand jury to determine whether it was sufficient to establish reasonable cause to warrant the return of the indictment. The court reversed the superior court's order, ruling that the grand jury had before it sufficient competent evidence to support the charge of conspiracy against all defendants. There was probable cause to determine that defendants knew the contents of the books and realized that such material could reasonably be regarded as obscene, establishing scienter under Cal. Penal Code § 311. The evidence presented to the grand jury justified the belief that the book deliveries were made at approximately the times alleged, and certainly within the three-year period of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order setting aside the conspiracy indictment against defendants.
